1 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Price


Docket No. 118613


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 118613; 76 N.E.3d 1240; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1517; 412 Ill. Dec. 782



December 30, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Price, 2014 IL App (1st) 130037-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2168 (Sept. 30, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where it could be argued that the State failed to pursue the timeliness issue, the Illinois Supreme Court had the authority to overlook any forfeiture in the interest of maintaining a sound and uniform body of precedent; [2]-Castleberry did not change any rule affecting the conduct of criminal prosecutions and came into play, if at all, only after judgment was rendered in the criminal trial; [3]-The Teague retroactivity analysis did not apply; [4]-The circuit court may treat a pro se petitioner's pleading, alleging a deprivation of a constitutional right, as a postconviction pleading although the pleading was not labeled as such.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

 

2 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Alvarez v. Gaughan


Docket No. 120110


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 120110; 72 N.E.3d 276; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1501; 410 Ill. Dec. 890



December 1, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Castleberry, 2013 IL App (1st) 111791-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2410 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The State's Attorney was granted a writ of mandamus under Ill. Const. art. VI, § 4(a) to compel the circuit judge to correct defendant's sentence with a mandatory 15-year firearm enhancement imposed on each of his two convictions for aggravated criminal sexual assault; [2]-Laches did not apply, because there was no unreasonable delay in the State's assertion of sentencing error and its attempt to rectify that error did not cause defendant to suffer prejudice; [3]-Pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/12-14(a)(8), (d)(1) (2008), two convictions based on two separate acts of sexual penetration while armed with a firearm warranted the imposition of two separate sentence enhancements; [4]-The State's Attorney from whose county the underlying criminal case arose had the authority and standing to bring the mandamus action under 55 ILCS 5/3-9005 (2014).


OUTCOME: Writ awarded.

 

3 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Blanchard v. Berrios


Docket No. 120315


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 120315; 72 N.E.3d 309; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1506; 410 Ill. Dec. 923



December 1, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Blanchard v. Berrios, 2015 IL App (1st) 142857, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 906, 400 Ill. Dec. 778, 48 N.E.3d 1218 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Cook County, Ill., Inspector General Ordinance (IG Ordinance), Cook County Code of Ordinances § 2-281 et seq. (2007), was not unconstitutional because Ill. Const. art. VII, § 4(d) did not bar making elected county officers cooperate with appellee, the Inspector General's, investigations; [2]-Enforcing Ill. Const. art. VII, § 4(d) did not conflict with the home rule article in Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6 because the IG Ordinance did not relate to property assessments or interfere with appellant Cook County, Ill., Assessor, its goal was within home rule units' Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(a) police power, and the County had an interest in detecting county government misconduct, which was not of statewide interest; [3]-The Assessor's election did not separate him from the County for home rule purposes because his office was part of the County, under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 1.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

4 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


Docket No. 119391


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 119391; 67 N.E.3d 256; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1233; 409 Ill. Dec. 44



October 20, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jones v. Ill., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 1864 (U.S., Mar. 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Jones, 2015 IL App (3d) 130053, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 380, 392 Ill. Dec. 198, 32 N.E.3d 198 (May 15, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's sentence to an extended-term sentence of 24 years' imprisonment based on a prior juvenile adjudication of delinquency referenced in his presentence investigative (PSI) report was proper because his prior juvenile adjudication was the equivalent of a prior conviction under Apprendi and fell within Apprendi's prior-conviction exception, as well as the exception in 725 ILCS 5/111-3(c-5) (2010); [2]-Defendant's PSI conclusively established the fact of his prior juvenile adjudication for residential burglary; [3]-Because defendant's delinquency proceedings did not involve any of the provision listed in , article V of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 ILCS 405/5-101 et seq. (2010), he did not have the right to a jury trial in those proceedings.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

5 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Minnis


Docket No. 119563


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 119563; 67 N.E.3d 272; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1235; 409 Ill. Dec. 60



October 20, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Minnis, 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1237 (Ill., Nov. 21, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Minnis v. Illinois, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 4195 (U.S., June 26, 2017)



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A finding that the Internet disclosure provisions under 730 ILCS 150/3(a) (2014), was overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I, was improper because the provisions advanced the substantial governmental interest of preventing sex offenses against children and protecting the public from the danger of recidivist sex offenders; [2]-The Internet disclosure provision survived intermediate scrutiny because it advanced a substantial governmental interest without chilling more speech than necessary; [3]-These disclosures empowered the public, if it wished, to make the informed decision to avoid such interactions; [4]-The information required for the public to protect itself was broad because any communication by a sex offender with the public is related to the statutory purpose.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

6 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Kakos v. Butler


Docket No. 120377


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 120377; 63 N.E.3d 901; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 774; 407 Ill. Dec. 469



September 22, 2016, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a medical negligence case where defendants filed a motion requesting a 12-person jury, the Illinois Supreme Court held that 2015 Ill. Laws 98-1132, which limited the size of a civil jury to 6 persons, was unconstitutional because it violated the common law right of trial by jury of twelve persons as guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 13; [2]-2015 Ill. Laws 98-1132, as it amends 735 ILCS 5/2-1105, is facially unconstitutional and void ab initio; [3]-The provision reducing the size of the jury cannot be severed from the remainder of 2015 Ill. Laws 98-1132, and therefore, the entirely of the act is invalid.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded.

 

7 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Reyes


Docket No. 119271


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 119271; 63 N.E.3d 884; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 770; 407 Ill. Dec. 452



September 22, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Reyes, 2015 IL App (2d) 120471, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 338, 400 Ill. Dec. 871, 49 N.E.3d 19 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment reversed. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because defendant was 16 years old at the time he committed the offenses, the sentencing scheme mandated that he remain in prison until at least the age of 105, and he would most certainly not live long enough to ever become eligible for release; [2]-Under these circumstances, defendant's term-of-years sentence was a mandatory, de facto life-without-parole sentence; [3]-By applying the new sentencing scheme of 730 ILCS 5/5-4.5-105 (Supp. 2015), the circuit court would have the discretion not to apply the firearm sentencing enhancements and, without these enhancements, the mandatory minimum aggregate sentence to which defendant would be subject was 32 years, a term that was not a de facto life sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

8 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hooker v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


121077


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 121077; 63 N.E.3d 824; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 1514; 407 Ill. Dec. 392



August 25, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied September 12, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Diane J. Larsen, Judge, presiding.
Hooker v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 2016 IL 121077, 2016 Ill. LEXIS 767 (2016)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Mandate to issue immediately.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court properly granted judgment on the pleadings, under 735 ILCS 5/2-615(e) (2014), holding a redistricting initiative petition did not comply with Ill. Const. art. XIV, § 3 because it was not limited to structural and procedural subjects in Ill. Const. art. IV, as it did not concern the structure of the legislature, it greatly expanded the duties assigned to the Auditor General by Ill. Const. art. VIII, § 3, materially affecting another section of the Illinois Constitution, and it was not explained how the Auditor General's hypothetical ability to perform the newly assigned tasks affected the proposal's constitutionality, whether or not it was designed intentionally to affect another constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

9 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Moline Sch. Dist. No. 40 Bd. of Educ. v. Quinn


(Docket No. 119704)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 119704; 54 N.E.3d 825; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 746; 403 Ill. Dec. 684



June 16, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Moline Sch. Dist. No. 40 Bd. of Educ. v. Quinn, 2015 IL App (3d) 140535, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 537, 394 Ill. Dec. 803, 37 N.E.3d 282 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Granting preferential property tax treatment to an aircraft support services company leasing property from a particular airport authority violated the prohibition against special legislation in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 because there was no reasonable basis for not providing tax incentives to similar businesses at other airports, absent evidence of any particular set of economic circumstances in the county that did not exist elsewhere or that would warrant special property tax incentives for businesses located there; [2]-Although encouraging business expansion in Illinois and facilitating economic growth were legitimate functions of state government, the challenged law did not require that the company actually use the tax savings to expand in Illinois, and other Illinois companies also would benefit from economic investment and job growth.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

10 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rizzo


(Docket No. 118599)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 118599; 61 N.E.3d 92; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 744; 406 Ill. Dec. 488



June 16, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rizzo v. Illinois, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 1371 (U.S., Feb. 21, 2017)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court erred in concluding that the prohibition of supervision as a disposition in 730 ILCS 5/5-6-1(p) (2012) was unconstitutional as violating Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 because while discussing what was "cruel" and "degrading," the circuit court's analysis actually used comparisons of the offense of speeding under 625 ILCS 5/11-601.5, and its prescribed "penalty" framework, with other offenses with different elements and the penalties assigned to them; the circuit court also improperly considered possible collateral consequences of the misdemeanor conviction.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

11 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. McFadden


(Docket No. 117424)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 117424; 61 N.E.3d 74; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 745; 406 Ill. Dec. 470



June 16, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McFadden v. Illinois, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 4107 (U.S., June 26, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. McFadden, 2014 IL App (1st) 102939, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 1087, 380 Ill. Dec. 259, 8 N.E.3d 429 (Nov. 30, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Circuit court judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's prior conviction for aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW) properly served as proof for his 2008 felony conviction for unlawful use of a weapon by a felon (UUW), in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1(a) (2008), because even if he was successful in vacating his conviction for AUUW under the void ab initio doctrine based on the declaration in Aguilar, the remedy would neither alter nor extinguish the requirement under § 24-1.1(a) that he clear his felon status before obtaining a firearm; [2]-A remand for resentencing on defendant's armed robbery convictions was not required; his concurrent sentences for committing armed robberies against three victims were 16 years below the maximum sentences permissible for those offenses, as provided in 730 ILCS 5/5-4.5-25(a).


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Richter v. Prairie Farms Dairy, Inc.


Docket No. 119518


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 119518; 53 N.E.3d 1; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 519; 402 Ill. Dec. 870



May 19, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Richter v. Prairie Farms Dairy, Inc., 2015 IL App (4th) 140613, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 429, 393 Ill. Dec. 416, 34 N.E.3d 617 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A refiled action by agricultural cooperative members (ACMs) against the AC, arising from the AC's termination of their membership, was improperly dismissed by the trial court pursuant to § 2-619 of the Code of Civil Procedure, 735 ILCS 5/2-619(a)(4) and (5) (2012), as the doctrine of res judicata did not bar the action because the dismissal order in the first action was not a final order under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 273 (eff. Jan. 1, 1967), in that it provided the ACMs with leave to file an amended complaint; [2]-Moreover, the action was not barred by the limitations period under 735 ILCS 5/13-205 (2012) because the limitations savings statute, 735 ILCS 5/13-217 (1994), permitted the refiled action, which was within the one-year refiling period.


OUTCOME: Judgment of appellate court affirmed; matter remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Hernandez


Docket No. 118672


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 118672; 51 N.E.3d 794; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 517; 402 Ill. Dec. 42



May 19, 2016, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in finding a proportionate penalties violation under the Illinois Constitution and erred in granting defendant a new sentencing hearing as relief on the proportionate penalties claim of his amended postconviction petition because the elements of armed robbery under 720 ILCS 5/18-2(a) (1998) were not identical to the elements of armed violence under 720 ILCS 5/33A-1, 33A-2 (1998), and the core prerequisite for invoking judicial estoppel did not exist.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Matthews v. Chi. Transit Auth.


Docket Nos. 117638, 117713, 117728 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 117638; 51 N.E.3d 753; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 508; 402 Ill. Dec. 1; 206 L.R.R.M. 3228; 166 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,705



May 5, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Matthews v. Chi. Transit Auth., 2014 IL App (1st) 123348, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 269, 381 Ill. Dec. 44, 9 N.E.3d 1163 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court erred in dismissing Class I plaintiff's claim for breach of contract and a violation of the pension protection clause in Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5, because the provision of health care benefits to plaintiffs who retired under 2004 CBA constituted an enforceable, vested right that survived expiration of that agreement; [2]-Because the retirees were not represented in the 2007 collective bargaining, they had standing to pursue claims for the enforcement of benefits granted under the CBA; [3]-The language of the pension protection clause in Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5 did not present an obstacle to a contractual provision that permitted subsequent modification of public retirement benefits; [4]-Plaintiff's promissory estoppel claim failed, because it sought to enforce a contractual obligation that went beyond the terms of the 2004 CBA.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded.

 

15 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Mun. Emples. Annuity & Ben. Fund of Chi.


(Docket Nos. 119618, 119620, 119638, 119639, 119644 cons.)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 119618; 50 N.E.3d 596; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 276; 401 Ill. Dec. 454



March 24, 2016, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5 removed the option of unilaterally diminishing pension benefits as a means of attaining pension stability; [2]-Whether members of the city pension funds may be better off under the new terms of 2014 Ill. Laws 98-641 despite the unconstitutional diminishment of their benefits was not for the General Assembly to decide unilaterally; [3]-The determination must be made, it at all, according to contract principles by mutual assent of the members, and not be legislative dictates; [4]-The unions were not acting as authorized agents within a collective bargaining process; [5]-The General Assembly would not have enacted 2014 Ill. Laws 98-641 without the invalid provisions, and the Act was unenforceable in its entirety.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

16 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Burns


(Docket No. 118973)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 118973; 50 N.E.3d 610; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 281; 401 Ill. Dec. 468



March 24, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Burns, 2015 IL App (4th) 140006, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 62, 389 Ill. Dec. 218, 25 N.E.3d 1244 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that the officers' warrantless use of a drug-detection dog at 3:20 a.m. at defendant's apartment door, located within a locked apartment building, violated defendant's rights under the Fourth Amendment; [2]-The good faith exception to the exclusionary rule under 725 ILCS 5/114-12(b)(1), (b)(2) (2012) did not apply because the officers could not have objectively, reasonably believed that their conduct was authorized under United State Supreme Court or Illinois Supreme Court precedent; [3]-The court held that absent the dog sniff, the evidence relied on in the complaint and affidavit for the search warrant was insufficient to establish probable cause for a search warrant for defendant's home, and therefore the trial court did not err by granting defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

17 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ligon


Docket No. 118023


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 118023; 48 N.E.3d 654; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 267; 400 Ill. Dec. 367



February 19, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Ligon, 2014 IL App (1st) 120913, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 426, 383 Ill. Dec. 214, 14 N.E.3d 497 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A defendant's eventual adjudication and sentence as an habitual criminal had no effect on a court's determination of whether a qualifying offense violated the proportionate penalties clause under the identical elements test; [2]-Defendant's BB gun could not be considered a bludgeon or other dangerous weapon of like character under the armed violence statute, but it did qualify as a dangerous weapon other than a firearm under the common-law definition applicable to statutory offenses such as aggravated vehicular hijacking and armed robbery; [3]-Defendant was properly convicted of aggravated vehicular hijacking with a dangerous weapon, other than a firearm, while using a BB gun as a common-law dangerous weapon of the third type. and it was irrelevant that the indictment used the term "bludgeon" instead of BB gun.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

 

18 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tolbert


Docket No. 117846


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2016 IL 117846; 49 N.E.3d 389; 2016 Ill. LEXIS 249; 401 Ill. Dec. 1



January 22, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Tolbert, 2016 Ill. LEXIS 284 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Tolbert, 2014 IL App (1st) 122343-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 940 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment vacated. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The invitee requirement of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(I) (2012), the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon statute, was not an element of the offense, but was an exception; [2]-Defendant therefore had to prove his entitlement to the exception, and the State had no obligation to include the invitee requirement in a charging instrument; [3]-There was express language in 720 ILCS 5/24-2(h) (2012) stating that the invitee requirement was meant to be an exemption, not an element.


OUTCOME: Appellate court judgment vacated; cause remanded.

 

19 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Michael D. (In re Michael D.)


Docket No. 119178


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 119178; 69 N.E.3d 822; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1507; 410 Ill. Dec. 277



December 17, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Michael D. (In re Michael D.), 2015 IL App (1st) 143181, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 183, 390 Ill. Dec. 870, 29 N.E.3d 1140 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Although the juvenile defendant argued that a final, appealable order was entered, he conceded that the trial court never made him a ward of the court; [2]-The final judgment in a juvenile delinquency case was the dispositional order, and the trial court did not enter a dispositional order; [3]-Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)'s provision granting the State the right to appeal suppression orders was not made applicable to juvenile cases through Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 660(a), and a suspension order entered in a juvenile case was not appealable under Rule 604(a); [4]-Juveniles placed under court suspension were not similarly situated to adult criminal defendants placed under suspension, and defendant could not make even the threshold showing necessary to establish an equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

20 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Burns


Docket No. 117387


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117387; 79 N.E.3d 159; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1511; 413 Ill. Dec. 810



December 17, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Burns, 2013 IL App (1st) 120929, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 929, 378 Ill. Dec. 552, 4 N.E.3d 151 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(d) (2008) of the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW) statute did not create separate and distinct offenses of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon, nor did making the sentence for a violation of the statute a Class 4 felony or a class 2 felony transform the offense of AUUW into a different form; [2]-The penalty enhancements in subsection (d) were not elements of the offense and did not come into play until after defendant was found guilty; [3]-The offense, as enacted by the legislature, did not include as an element of the offense the fact that the offender had a prior felony conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

 

21 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schweihs


Docket No. 117789


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117789; 43 N.E.3d 979; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1500; 398 Ill. Dec. 69



December 3, 2015, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Contrary to the circuit court's ruling, the location element in 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1) (2012) of the Aggravated Unlawful Use of a Weapon (AUUW) statute was constitutional and enforceable when combined with subsection (a)(3)(C); [2]-When a defendant's conduct violated more than one statute, each of which required different proof, a defendant was not denied equal protection if he was prosecuted under the statute which provided the greater penalty.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

22 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompson


Docket No. 118151


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 118151; 43 N.E.3d 984; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1495; 398 Ill. Dec. 74



December 3, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Thompson, 2014 IL App (1st) 121729-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1312 (2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant convicted of two counts of first-degree murder was not permitted to raise an as-applied constitutional challenge to his mandatory natural life sentence for the first time on appeal from the circuit court's dismissal of his petition for relief from judgment under 735 ILCS 5/2-1401, as the void ab initio doctrine did not apply; [2]-Defendant's 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 petition was filed 17 years after his conviction and sentence, well outside the two-year limitations period; [3]-Defendant's claim was not exempt from the typical procedural bars of 735 ILCS 5/2-1401; [4]-Defendant's claim needed to be presented to a trial court, as the record on appeal did not contain any factual development on the issue of whether Miller should be extended to ban mandatory natural life sentences to a defendant who was between the ages of 18 and 21 when the crime was committed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

23 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


Docket No. 117470


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117470; 43 N.E.3d 941; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1275; 398 Ill. Dec. 31



November 19, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Williams, 2015 Ill. LEXIS 13 (Ill., Jan. 13, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed. Cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because the offense of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW) and a violation of the Firearm Owner's Identification Card (FOID Card) Act were not identical, there could be no proportionate penalty violation; [2]-A person could violate the FOID Card Act by possessing a firearm in his home without also having in possession a FOID card, whereas such conduct would not violate the AUUW statute, because the offense of AUUW required proof of the additional element that a person be outside his home or on the public way; [3]-The identical elements test simply compared the elements of the two offenses to determine if they were the same, and the objective test did not consider the offenses as applied to an individual defendant.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

24 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Matthew A. (In re A.A.)


Docket No. 118605


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 118605; 43 N.E.3d 947; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1276; 398 Ill. Dec. 37



November 19, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Matthew A. (In re A.A.), 2014 IL App (5th) 140252, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 752, 386 Ill. Dec. 364, 20 N.E.3d 526 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An action brought under the Illinois Parentage Act on behalf of a minor to declare the nonexistence of a parent and child relationship did not provide for the court to consider the best interests of the child prior to granting the petition; [2]-The Parentage Act contained no express requirement that a court consider the best interests of the child before any testing was conducted or a legal determination of paternity was made, as the first step in the proceeding was to establish or disestablish parentage.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

25 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Castleberry


Docket No. 116916


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 116916; 43 N.E.3d 932; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1273; 398 Ill. Dec. 22



November 19, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Castleberry, 2013 IL App (1st) 111791-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2410 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Sentence imposed without the statutory enhancement was not void because, under Ill. Const. art. VI, § 9, the "void sentence rule," which states that a sentence which does not conform to a statutory requirement is void, is abolished. (People v. Arna, 168 Ill. 2d 107 (1995), is overruled insofar as it is inconsistent); [2]-Appellate court could not increase defendant's sentence at the request of the State because the State's argument was a de facto cross-appeal under Ill. S. Ct. R. 604(a) challenging defendant's sentence and, as such, was impermissible; further, under Ill. S. Ct. R. 615(b)(1), (4), the appellate court could not increase the sentence on review.


OUTCOME: Circuit court judgment affirmed and appellate court judgment reversed.

 

26 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. M.A. (In re M.A.)


Docket No. 118049


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 118049; 43 N.E.3d 86; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1263; 397 Ill. Dec. 759



November 4, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. M.A. (In re M.A.), 2014 IL App (1st) 132540, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 362, 382 Ill. Dec. 526, 12 N.E.3d 805 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Court properly required the juvenile defendant to register under 730 ILCS 154/10(a), 40 (2012) and Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 1283.50(j) (2010) because the defendant's rights to substantive due process, procedural due process, and equal protection under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 were not violated; the Murderer and Violent Offender Against Youth Registration Act does not violate substantive due process, procedural due process, or equal protection.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

27 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Folta v. Ferro Eng'g


Docket No. 118070


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 118070; 43 N.E.3d 108; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1264; 397 Ill. Dec. 781



November 4, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Folta v. Ferro Eng'g, 2014 IL App (1st) 123219, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 444, 383 Ill. Dec. 434, 14 N.E.3d 717 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-820 ILCS 305/5(a), 820 ILCS 305/11, 820 ILCS 310/5(a), and 820 ILCS 310/11 (2010) barred appellee, a deceased employee's estate's, asbestos claim against appellant employer, because their statute of repose expired before the disease appeared, and the lack of a remedy created no exclusivity exception; [2]-The disease's appearance after the 820 ILCS 310/1(f) (2010) time limit did not allow common law recovery because that time limit did not remove occupational diseases from the Workers' Compensation Act or the Workers' Occupational Diseases Act; [3]-Equal protection under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and the special legislation bar in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 were not violated because no "categorical" class was denied a right to seek benefits; [4]-The right to a certain remedy in Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 was not violated because no remedy against third parties was barred.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

 

28 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Price v. Philip Morris, Inc.


Docket No. 117687


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117687; 43 N.E.3d 53; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 1265; 397 Ill. Dec. 726



November 4, 2015, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Price v. Philip Morris, Inc., 2016 U.S. LEXIS 4032 (U.S., June 20, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Price v. Philip Morris, Inc., 2014 IL App (5th) 130017, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 279, 380 Ill. Dec. 928, 9 N.E.3d 599 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgments vacated. Cause dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2012) did not authorize a circuit court to grant collateral relief from a judgment of a reviewing court, neither the circuit court, nor the appellate court on review, had the authority to vacate the judgment of the court rendered on December 15, 2005; [2]-Whether the prayer in plaintiffs' § 2-1401 petition to vacate the final judgment was viewed as a request to the circuit court to vacate the December 15, 2005 judgment of the court, or a request to vacate the December 18, 2006 dismissal order on the merits, the result was the same because the circuit court was asked to do something it did not have the authority to do, vacate a judgment of a higher court; because relief was unavailable under § 2-1401, the petition should have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: Judgments vacated. Cause dismissed.

 

29 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


McElwain v. Office of the Ill. Secy. of State


(Docket No. 117170)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117170; 39 N.E.3d 550; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 775; 396 Ill. Dec. 1



September 24, 2015, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-On appeal of the order denying plaintiff's request for rescission of license suspension, the court held that 625 ILCS 5/11-501.6 (2012) was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff because the police sought a chemical test two days after the car accident when plaintiff no longer had a diminished expectation of privacy; [2]-A chemical test requested two days after the accident, rather than shortly after the accident, is obviously much less probative of the question whether the person was driving while impaired; [3]-Even assuming 625 ILCS 5/11-501.6 is facially valid under the unconstitutional conditions test for having a driver's license requires implied consent to a chemical test after a serious accident, 625 ILCS 5/11-501.6 was applied to plaintiff in an unconstitutional manner.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

30 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. McGuire


Docket No. 117138


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117138; 39 N.E.3d 982; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 772; 396 Ill. Dec. 156



September 24, 2015, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Walker v. Ocwen Loan Servicing, LLC, 2016 IL App (3d) 150034-U, 2016 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1063 (2016)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Ill. Const. art. VI, § 14 (1970) was ambiguous; [2]-No change in meaning was intended with the change in language in the 1970 provision, and the 1964 provision considered masters in chancery; [3]-Clerks of the circuit courts did not fall within the ambit of art. VI, § 14 as they were nonjudicial officers under 705 ILCS 105/13 (2012) and performed no adjudicative or quasi-judicial functions; [4]-The judicial fee officer prohibition did not apply to the clerks of the circuit courts, and 735 ILCS 5/15-1504.1 (2012) did not create an impermissible fee office; [5]-The purpose of the Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a) appeal was fulfilled by the reversal of the unconstitutionality holding; [6]-Plaintiff did not amend his complaint to challenge the amended statutes, or to add additional named plaintiffs; [7]-The trial court's ruling was properly limited to § 15-1504.1 (2012).


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

31 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. LeFlore


Docket No. 116799


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 116799; 32 N.E.3d 1043; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 510; 392 Ill. Dec. 467



May 21, 2015, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Leflore v. Ill., 2015 U.S. LEXIS 4845 (U.S., Oct. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. LeFlore, 2013 IL App (2d) 100659, 996 N.E.2d 678, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 636, 374 Ill. Dec. 983 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The good faith exception to the exclusionary rule was applicable and therefore the appellate court erred by vacating the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence that was obtained as a result of a detective's installation and use of a GPS device on defendant's vehicle because at the time of the detective's conduct in April 2009 the United States Supreme Court's decisions in Knotts and Karo, which held that warrantless installation and monitoring of a beeper signal was legal, were binding appellate precedent that the detective could have reasonably relied upon, the police conduct in relying on the legal landscape that existed at the time was objectively reasonable, and there was a complete lack of police culpability and there would be little or no deterrent value to suppressing the evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, case remanded.

 

32 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Richardson


Docket No. 118255


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 118255; 32 N.E.3d 666; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 501; 392 Ill. Dec. 358



May 21, 2015, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant was charged with two counts of criminal sexual assault for acts he allegedly committed when he was 17 years old, the saving clause in the exclusive jurisdiction provision of the Illinois Juvenile Court Act, 705 ILCS 405/5-120, did not violate his rights under the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV; [2]-At the time of defendant's offense in 2012, the Illinois Juvenile Court Act only applied to those minors who were under 17 years of age; [3]-Effective 2014, the exclusive jurisdiction provision of the Juvenile Court Act, 705 ILCS 405/5-120 (Supp. 2013), was amended to apply to minors who were under 18 years of age; [4]-It was reasonable for the legislature to distinguish between offenses committed before and offenses committed after the amendment's effective date.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

33 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gaytan


Docket No. 116223


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 116223; 32 N.E.3d 641; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 502; 392 Ill. Dec. 333



May 21, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Gaytan, 2013 IL App (4th) 120217, 992 N.E.2d 17, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 374, 372 Ill. Dec. 478 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where police stopped defendant's car, erroneously believing that the trailer hitch obstructed the vehicle's license plate in violation of 625 ILCS 5/3-413(b) (2010), the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress cannabis found in the car because the officers' objectively reasonable mistake of law provided the reasonable suspicion necessary to justify the stop under the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV; [2]-625 ILCS 5/3-413(b) prohibits only those objects that obstruct the visibility of the license plate which are physically connected or attached to the plate itself; [3]-An objectively reasonable, though mistaken, belief as to the meaning of a law may form the basis for a constitutionally valid vehicle stop under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6.


OUTCOME: Appellate court reversed, and circuit court affirmed.

Marks v. Vanderventer


Docket Nos. 116226, 116825 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 116226; 39 N.E.3d 915; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 503; 396 Ill. Dec. 89



May 21, 2015, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Marks v. Vanderventer, 2015 Ill. LEXIS 780 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A Rental Housing Support Program surcharge collected by a recorder of deeds pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/3-5018 (Supp. 2013) was not unconstitutional under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) because the recorder neither retained the dollar nor had discretion to determine how it was spent; [2]-Moreover, 55 ILCS 5/3-5018 (Supp. 2013) did not constitute a fee for the collection of taxes imposed by another governmental body; [3]-55 ILCS 5/3-5018 (Supp. 2013) did not violate the uniformity clause under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 if there was a reasonable relationship between the object of the legislation and the classification at issue; [4]-55 ILCS 5/3-5018 (Supp. 2013) did not violate due process under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 under rational basis review, and there was no need to reach the merits of an equal protection challenge.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

Heaton v. Quinn (In re Pension Reform Litig.)


Docket No. 118585


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 118585; 32 N.E.3d 1; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 499; 392 Ill. Dec. 1; 165 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,590



May 8, 2015, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In enacting the annuity reduction provisions of Illinois Public Act 98-599 (2014), the Illinois General Assembly overstepped the scope of its legislative power as there was no way that the provisions could be reconciled with the rights and protections established by the people of Illinois when they ratified the Illinois Constitution and its pension protection clause, Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5; hence, the Act was void and unenforceable in its entirety.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

36 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Leetaru v. Bd. of Trs. of the Univ. of Ill.


Docket No. 117485


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117485; 32 N.E.3d 583; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 485; 392 Ill. Dec. 275



April 16, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Leetaru v. Bd. of Trs. of the Univ. of Ill., 2014 IL App (4th) 130465, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 81, 378 Ill. Dec. 934, 5 N.E.3d 314 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because sovereign immunity under the State Lawsuit Immunity Act, 745 ILCS 5/0.01 et seq. (2012), and Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 4 afforded no protection under the ultra vires exception when state agents acted in violation of statutory or constitutional law or in excess of their authority, which was what a graduate student alleged in a suit seeking to compel state university administrators to adhere to the policies and procedures promulgated by the university governing misconduct investigations, the student was not required under 705 ILCS 505/8(a) (2012) to proceed in the Court of Claims; [2]-Accordingly, the student was entitled to proceed in circuit court regardless of whether the suit was authorized under the sue and be sued provision in 110 ILCS 305/1 (2012) or whether the suit implicated the student's right to access to the courts under Ill. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

37 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Madigan v. J.T. Einoder, Inc.


Docket No. 117193


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117193; 28 N.E.3d 758; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 324; 390 Ill. Dec. 105



March 19, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People ex rel. Madigan v. J.T. Einoder, Inc., 2013 IL App (1st) 113498, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 864, 377 Ill. Dec. 816, 2 N.E.3d 1097 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In accordance with the prohibition in 5 ILCS 70/4 (2000) against retroactivity of substantive amendments, 415 ILCS 5/42(e) (2004) could not be applied retroactively to authorize mandatory injunctive relief for environmental violations because that remedy was not available prior to the amendment of § 42(e) and the amendment thus created a new type of liability; [2]-Even if a corporate officer had not been part of the day-to-day operations, the circuit court did not manifestly err in ruling that the officer's involvement in site operations was sufficiently demonstrated by the officer's authorization of contracts for dumping at the site, and the officer thus was properly held individually liable for operating a waste disposal facility without a permit under 415 ILCS 5/21(d) (2000) and depositing clean construction and demolition debris above grade.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.

James R.D. v. Maria Z. (In re Scarlett Z.-D.)


Docket No. 117904


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117904; 28 N.E.3d 776; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 321; 390 Ill. Dec. 123



March 19, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: James R.D. v. Maria Z. (In re Scarlett Z.-D.), 2014 IL App (2d) 120266-B, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 346, 381 Ill. Dec. 729, 11 N.E.3d 360 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The child's adoptive mother did not forfeit the opportunity to contest her ex-fiance's standing to seek custody of the child because her 735 ILCS 5/2-619 (2012) motion was timely as it was filed well within the time for pleading and prior to evidentiary hearings; [2]-The mother was not equitably estopped from challenging her ex-fiance's standing to seek custody, visitation, and child support because the record contained no evidence that the mother misrepresented to her ex-fiance that he was the child's biological or adoptive father and when the parties terminated their relationship the mother's assertion was not inconsistent with or a repudiation of her prior behavior; [3]-The ex-fiance could not state an equitable claim for custody, visitation, and support based on functional parent theories because they were not recognized by Illinois.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment vacated. Cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The provisions of the Collection Agency Act applied to entities such as the collection agency, 225 ILCS 425/3(d) (2008), because it identified itself as an assignee of the bank and was subject to the registration requirement of 225 ILCS 425/4 (2008); [2]-The collection agency's failure to register as a debt collection agency was error, but any error in failing to register did not deprive the circuit court of jurisdiction, and the circuit court's judgment was not void; [3]-The circuit court's initial denial of the debtor's 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008) petition was correct.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated and remanded.

People v. Mosley


Docket No. 115872


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 115872; 33 N.E.3d 137; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 303; 392 Ill. Dec. 588



February 20, 2015, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Mosley, 2015 Ill. LEXIS 740 (Ill., June 5, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-It was proper to vacate a conviction under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(A) for carrying on the person or in any vehicle, outside the home, a firearm that was uncased, loaded, and immediately accessible because during the pendency of appeal, the court found that provision to violate the right to keep and bear arms under U.S. Const. amend. II; [2]-The same conduct cannot be barred when the alleged offender similarly carries a firearm on a public way; [3]-No violation of the right to bear arms arose from convictions under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (2) and (a)(3)(C) for possessing a firearm while outside the home and on a public way, while without a firearm owner identification card and while being under 21 years of age and not engaged in lawful hunting activities; [4]-No equal protection violation arose from treating individuals over and under 21 years of age differently.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

People v. Jordan G. (In re Jordan G.)


Docket No. 116834


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 116834; 33 N.E.3d 162; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 306; 392 Ill. Dec. 613



February 20, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Jordan G. (In re Jordan G.), 2015 Ill. LEXIS 16 (Ill., Jan. 13, 2015)

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The legislature would find that 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(3)(C) and (a)(3)(I) could stand independently, and severing subsection (a)(3)(A) undermined neither the completeness of, nor the ability to, execute the remaining subsections; [2]-The possession of handguns by minors was conduct that fell outside the scope of U.S. Const. amend. II's protection, and neither subsection (a)(3)(C) nor (a)(3)(I) violated the Second Amendment rights of 18-20 year-old persons; [3]-Whether legislation prohibiting those who had previously been adjudicated delinquent from possessing firearms would comport with the Second Amendment was not before the appellate court.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

42 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Grand Chapter, Order of the Eastern Star v. Topinka


Docket No. 117083


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117083; 25 N.E.3d 621; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 24; 388 Ill. Dec. 929



January 23, 2015, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The purpose of the bed fee, 305 ILCS 5/5E-10 (2012), was not simply to fund Medicaid but served many additional purposes that were wholly unrelated to the Medicaid program; [2]-Under 305 ILCS 5/5B-8 (2012), each of the purposes may be funded by the bed fee, and not one of them was tied in any way directly to the Medicaid program; [3]-The operative inquiry in uniformity cases was not whether there was perfect reciprocity between payment of the tax and distribution of the tax, but rather only whether the taxing classification bore some reasonable relationship to the object or purpose of the tax; [4]-Everyone who lived in Illinois benefited from and had an interest in ensuring that Illinois's bond obligations remained adequately funded, and the bed fees deposited into the Long-Term Care Provider Fund were available for this purpose.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

People v. Taylor


Docket No. 117267


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2015 IL 117267; 25 N.E.3d 627; 2015 Ill. LEXIS 26; 388 Ill. Dec. 935



January 23, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Taylor, 2013 IL App (4th) 110633-UB, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2983 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-At the time defendant committed the crime, the enhanced sentence for armed robbery with a firearm violated the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, and because defendant committed the crime and was sentenced prior to the amendment of 2007 Ill. Laws 95-688, the sentencing enhancement was disproportionate when applied and the sentence was facially unconstitutional and void; [2]-Defendant did not argue that his sentence was excessive in light of the crime committed and the appellate court had no evidence that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing a 24-year sentence and it would not be appropriate for the appellate court to reduce that sentence; [3]-Imposing a sentence cap at 24 years would be premature, and the circuit court had to determine whether it was appropriate to sentence defendant to a prison term greater than 24 years.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because petitioner's case fell within the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine, the court addressed the merits of his request for mandamus relief even though he had already been released from mandatory supervised release (MSR); [2]-Petitioner did not establish that he was entitled to a writ of mandamus because he failed to show that respondents had the authority, let alone a duty, to order his release to serve his MSR under 730 ILCS 5/5-8-1(d) (2012) when no suitable host location had been found; although he claimed he was denied MSR based upon indigency, it appeared that the Illinois Department of Corrections was unable to find a placement for him due to his status as a sex offender, rather than his status as an indigent.

46 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Pusateri v. Peoples Gas Light & Coke Co.


Docket No. 116844


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2014 IL 116844; 21 N.E.3d 437; 2014 Ill. LEXIS 1321; 386 Ill. Dec. 674



November 20, 2014, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: State ex rel. Pusateri v. People Gas Light & Coke Co., 2013 IL App (1st) 120972-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2153 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-No part of the False Claims Act (Act), 740 ILCS 175/4 (2008), enlarged the subject matter jurisdiction of the circuit courts, and nothing in the Act indicated an intent to abridge or disturb the Illinois Commerce Commission's (Commission) exclusive jurisdiction; [2]-Outside the administrative review prescribed by 220 ILCS 5/10-201 (2008), the circuit court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to adjudicate the central question of the consumer's complaint: whether the rate set by the Commission was too high by virtue of the allegedly false gas leak reports, and the circuit court was further unable to offer reparations; [3]-The legsilature enacted the False Claims Act long after the findings about the exclusive jurisdiction of the Commission, and there was no indication that the legislature intended to abridge that jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

2014 IL 116642; 21 N.E.3d 418; 2014 Ill. LEXIS 1322; 386 Ill. Dec. 655



November 20, 2014, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because it was a proceeding under the Public Utilities Act, the appeal was governed by 220 ILCS 5/10-201 (2010), and the 35-day statutory period was controlling and there was no dispute that the State filed its appeal within the statutory period; [2]-Ill. R. 303(a) whenever review of administrative orders was within the appellate court; [3]-The statutory period set forth in 220 ILCS 5/10-201(a) controlled and should have been given effect by the appellate court.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

Hiroshi Hayashi v. Ill. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation


Docket Nos. 116023, 116163, 116190 cons


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2014 IL 116023; 25 N.E.3d 570; 2014 Ill. LEXIS 1311; 388 Ill. Dec. 878



October 17, 2014, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hiroshi Hayashi v. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 2015 Ill. LEXIS 35 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hiroshi Hayashi v. Ill. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 4223 (U.S., June 22, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consiglio v. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 2013 IL App (1st) 121142, 988 N.E.2d 1020, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 215, 370 Ill. Dec. 664 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Phrase "has been convicted," as used in 20 ILCS 2105/2105-165(a) refers to health care workers who hold the status of having been convicted of a particular offense, no matter when that status was obtained. The plain language of the provision clearly applied to convictions imposed prior to its effective date; [2]-In the context of substantive due process, the provision is solely prospective and not retroactive in its operation; [3]-Plaintiffs had not alleged a substantive due process violation based on the revocation of their health care licenses pursuant to the provision; [4]-Plaintiffs had received all of the process that they were due and failed to allege a procedural due process violation either facially or as applied; [5]-Res judicata did not apply in the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The Court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which affirmed the circuit court's judgments holding that plaintiffs' complaints were properly dismissed pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-615.

 

49 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Patterson


Docket No. 115102


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2014 IL 115102; 25 N.E.3d 526; 2014 Ill. LEXIS 1313; 388 Ill. Dec. 834



October 17, 2014, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Patterson, 2015 Ill. LEXIS 33 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Patterson v. Illinois, 136 S. Ct. 399, 193 L. Ed. 2d 313, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 6846 (U.S., 2015)
On remand at, Remanded by, Decision reached on appeal by People v. Patterson, 2016 IL App (1st) 101573-B, 2016 Ill. App. LEXIS 383 (2016)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Patterson, 2016 IL App (1st) 101573-B, 2016 Ill. App. LEXIS 753 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Patterson, 2012 IL App (1st) 101573, 975 N.E.2d 1127, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 800, 363 Ill. Dec. 818 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A juvenile defendant's statement was not involuntary by reason of the youth officer's participation and the absence of a concerned adult because the police made adequate efforts to notify a concerned adult under 705 ILCS 405/5-405(2) (2008) by leaving voicemail messages and the totality of the circumstances did not indicate that defendant was coerced or confused; [2]-Counsel was not ineffective because the admission of defendant's confession was not prejudicial in light of physical evidence strongly corroborating the victim's testimony; [3]-A transfer to adult court under 705 ILCS 405/5-130 (2008) did not violate due process, and because it was procedural rather than punitive, U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 were not implicated; [4]-The rape shield statute, 725 ILCS 5/115-7(a) (2008), was properly applied absent a sufficient offer of proof.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

65 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hope Clinic for Women, Ltd. v. Flores


Docket Nos. 112673, 112704 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 112673; 991 N.E.2d 745; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 846; 372 Ill. Dec. 255



July 11, 2013, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Hope Clinic for Women Ltd. v. Adams, 2011 IL App (1st) 101463, 955 N.E.2d 511, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 649, 353 Ill. Dec. 44 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff clinic and physician challenged the Parental Notice of Abortion Act of 1995, 750 ILCS 70/1 et seq., as unconstitutional on its face. The Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, reversed the lower court, finding that the Act was unconstitutional. Petitions for leave to appeal were granted and the cases were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The right to an abortion in Illinois law was not grounded in the Privacy Clause, Ill. Const. art. I. § 6. Rather, a state constitutional right to abortion derived from Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, which was interpreted equivalent to the due process protections of the Fourteenth Amendment. The Act did not violate the right to privacy where the intrusion into a minor's privacy was not unreasonable given that it required the minor to give notice to only one legally responsible adult and provided for an exception to the notice requirement when a medical emergency existed. Thus, the Act was narrowly crafted to achieve its aim of promoting the minors' best interests through parental consultation. The Act did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, given that parental notification served compelling state interests. The Act also did not violate Ill. Const. art. I. § 18, as the Act did not create a sex-based classification.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed in part and affirmed in part. The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

 

66 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. M.I. (In re M.I.)


Docket No. 113776


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 113776; 989 N.E.2d 173; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 567; 370 Ill. Dec. 785



May 23, 2013, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by M. I. v. Illinois, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7557 (U.S., Oct. 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. M.I. (In re M.I.), 968 N.E.2d 82, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 603, 360 Ill. Dec. 3 (Ill., 2012)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile was adjudicated delinquent for weapons offenses. The trial court granted the State's motion to designate the proceedings as an extended jurisdiction juvenile prosecution under 705 ILCS 405/5-810 (2008). The trial court imposed an indeterminate juvenile sentence and an adult sentence of 23 years in prison. The Appellate Court of Illinois affirmed. The state supreme court allowed respondent's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Prior respondent's delinquency adjudication, the State filed a motion to designate the proceedings as an extended jurisdiction juvenile (EJJ) prosecution pursuant to the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 ILCS 405/5-810 (2008). The Supreme Court of Illinois held that the statutory requirement to hold a hearing within 60 days of the filing of an EJJ motion was directory; therefore, the trial court's failure to hold a hearing within 60 days did not void the stayed adult sentence. Because respondent received notice of the EJJ motion filing and a hearing on the motion in accordance with 705 ILCS 405/5-810(2), his rights were not prejudiced. Finally, the EJJ statute did not violate due process under Apprendi. There was nothing in the EJJ statute that allowed a juvenile to be sentenced above the statutory maximum based on factors not proven to a trier of fact beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

67 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Colyar


Docket No. 111835


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 111835; 996 N.E.2d 575; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 554; 374 Ill. Dec. 880



April 18, 2013, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Colyar, 2013 IL 111835, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 1353, 374 Ill. Dec. 880 (Ill., Oct. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Colyar, 407 Ill. App. 3d 294, 941 N.E.2d 479, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1423, 346 Ill. Dec. 921 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed a judgment that granted defendant's motion to suppress all evidence recovered from his vehicle after police investigated why his running vehicle was blocking the entrance to a motel parking lot, and conducted a protective search upon seeing in plain view a bullet sticking up inside a plastic bag in its center console. The state supreme court granted the State's motion for leave to appeal that ruling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple weapons charges after police officers recovered bullets and a handgun from his person and vehicle when they investigated why his vehicle was blocking the entrance to a motel parking lot. Defendant filed a pretrial motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence, and argued that the underlying search, prompted by the officers seeing a plastic bag in the center console of his vehicle that contained a bullet sticking up inside it, was unreasonable in violation of his Fourth Amendment rights and that he was subjected to an unlawful arrest without probable cause. The trial court granted his motion to suppress all evidence recovered, which consisted of additional bullets and a handgun. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court disagreed with both the trial and appellate courts. It found that after the officers saw the bullet in plain view, they had a reasonable concern for their own safety and could conduct the protective searches that occurred, even without probable cause. It added that they did not have to first ask defendant whether he had a valid FOID card before conducting the search.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the judgments of the appellate court and the trial court.

People v. Fitzpatrick


Docket No. 113449


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 113449; 986 N.E.2d 1163; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 545; 369 Ill. Dec. 527



April 4, 2013, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Fitzpatrick, 2011 IL App (2d) 100463, 960 N.E.2d 709, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1144, 355 Ill. Dec. 827 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress cocaine that was discovered during a search of his person after he was arrested for a petty offense. The Appellate Court, Second District (Illinois), affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress because an arrest for a petty offense was not unreasonable under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6, and therefore the cocaine was properly discovered during the search incident to defendant's arrest. In Atwater, the United States Supreme Court held that an arrest for a minor, fine-only offense was not unreasonable under the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court held that under the limited lockstep doctrine, it construed Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 the same way because defendant failed to show that any of the narrow exceptions to lockstep interpretation applied. Illinois had no common law or statutory tradition of prohibiting arrests for minor offenses. The court held that defendant forfeited his claim that the appellate court erred by remanding the case for a hearing on his ability to pay a public defender fee by failing to raise it in his petition for leave to appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

69 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Blair


Docket No. 114122


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 114122; 986 N.E.2d 75; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 306; 369 Ill. Dec. 126



March 21, 2013, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Blair, 2012 IL App (3d) 100743-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 102 (2012)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court reversed the trial court's finding that 2007 Ill. Laws 95-688, amending the armed violence statute, revived a sentencing enhancement in the armed robbery statute that the state supreme court had held unconstitutional. In the case, defendant had been convicted of armed robbery while armed with a firearm, 720 ILCS 5/18-2(a)(2) (2008). The state supreme court allowed the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery while armed with a firearm in violation of 720 ILCS 5/18-2(a)(2) (2008). The trial court sentenced defendant to a term of 23 years in prison, which included a 15-year enhancement under 720 ILCS 5/18-2(b) (2008). On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court erred by applying the 15-year enhancement upon rejecting the State's claim a Public Act had revived the sentencing enhancement in the armed robbery statute by amending the armed violence statute. It remanded for a resentencing that did not include the enhancement. The state supreme court found that the legislature's enactment of 2007 Ill. Laws 95-688 after the state supreme court found the enhancement unconstitutional in Hauschild was an amendment to the comparison statute, the armed violence statute, and had the effect of reviving the firearm enhancement for armed robbery with a firearm because it eliminated any issue regarding identical offense elements. In so holding, it rejected defendant's claim that no revival had occurred, as it found the amendment had not made the enhancement statute void ab initio, which a reviewing court could not do, but, rather, unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Eppinger


Docket No. 114121


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 114121; 984 N.E.2d 475; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 270; 368 Ill. Dec. 529



February 22, 2013, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court Third District.
People v. Eppinger, 2012 IL App (3d) 100577-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 450 (2012)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed. Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, two counts of armed robbery, and unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon, and was sentenced to 95 years' imprisonment. The Illinois Court of Appeals reversed and remanded for a new trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court properly remanded for a new trial because he was statutorily entitled to appointment of counsel, i.e., once defendant decided not to participate in his trial by refusing to leave his holding cell, the circuit court had no choice, pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/115-4.1, but to appoint counsel before proceeding with the trial. The supreme court disagreed and held that 725 ILCS 5/115-4.1 was inapplicable to in-custody defendants. Accordingly, the trial court was not statutorily required to appoint a third public defender and continue the trial date simply because defendant, after waiving his right to counsel, decided to waive also his right to be present by refusing to leave his holding cell. In other words, express statutory authority was not a prerequisite to trial in absentia. Defendant made no constitutionally based argument that required appointment of counsel in the face of a valid waiver of that right. Instead, defendant's claim of error was based entirely on 725 ILCS 5/115-4.1, which was inapplicable under the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed. The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

71 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jackson


Docket No. 113986


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 113986; 983 N.E.2d 1027; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 265; 368 Ill. Dec. 223



February 7, 2013, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Circuit Court of Clinton County.


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clinton County Circuit Court, Illinois, granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge on the ground that 625 ILCS 5/6-303 (2010) was unconstitutional as applied to him. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the question to be resolved was one concerning proof of the elements of the offense and not, as the circuit court found, a question of constitutionality of the statute defining the offense. The supreme court found that the State may rebut defendant's evidence that he possessed a valid license with evidence that his license was not valid because he purposely misled the authorities to prevent them from properly determining that his driving privileges had not been otherwise suspended, revoked, or cancelled. In a trial for a violation of 625 ILCS 5/6-303, the case law and statutory scheme for restoring suspended and revoked licenses allowed for a determination by the trier of fact as to whether the defendant misled authorities into reinstating his privilege to drive by providing erroneous information through either purposeful concealment or incorrect representation. There was no affirmative defense to violations of that section where the defendant did not contest that his license was suspended or revoked.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

72 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. English


Docket No. 112890


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2013 IL 112890; 987 N.E.2d 371; 2013 Ill. LEXIS 7; 369 Ill. Dec. 744



January 25, 2013, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. English, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 552 (Ill., Apr. 18, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District.
People v. English, 2011 IL App (3d) 100764, 952 N.E.2d 677, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 687, 351 Ill. Dec. 885 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of felony murder under 720 ILCS 5/9-1(a)(3) (1994) and aggravated battery of a child under 720 ILCS 5/12-4.3(a) (1994). He was sentenced to mandatory natural life imprisonment. The circuit court denied his postconviction petition. The Appellate Court of Illinois affirmed. The state supreme court allowed his timely petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court did not err in denying appellant's petition for relief under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq. (2010), because the issue of whether the aggravated battery of a child could properly serve as the predicate felony for felony murder was available to him at the time of his direct appeal. Accordingly, appellant's argument was forfeited. The Supreme Court of Illinois held that his counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise the issue on direct appeal. He conceded that the basis on which he sought to invalidate his murder conviction, the independent felonious purpose analysis, was not supported by precedent at the time of his direct appeal. Consequently, it was reasonable for appellate counsel to conclude that the issue was unlikely to succeed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

73 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Carr v. Koch


Docket No. 113414


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2012 IL 113414; 981 N.E.2d 326; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1529; 367 Ill. Dec. 1



November 29, 2012, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Carr v. Koch, 960 N.E.2d 640, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1121, 355 Ill. Dec. 758, 2011 IL App (4th) 110117 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Sangamon County, Illinois, dismissed plaintiff taxpayers' declaratory judgment seeking a declaration that the Illinois Education funding system set forth in 105 ILCS 5/18-8.05 (2010) (education funding statute) violated the equal protection clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The appellate court affirmed. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that they had standing to challenge the state's educational funding system, and that their complaint stated a claim for violation of the equal protection clause. The supreme court agreed with the appellate court that the taxpayers' allegations failed to establish that their alleged injury was a direct result of the enforcement of the education funding statute or was fairly traceable to defendants', State Board of Education officials and Governor, actions. The school districts and not defendants controlled the amount of local property taxes imposed. The taxpayers' claims that the imposition of the higher taxes as a direct result of the enforcement of the statute and was fairly traceable to defendants was too attenuated to confer standing. The education funding statute did not require or compel school districts to tax at a certain rate, nor did it require school districts to reach the Foundation Level in order to receive the general state aid to which they were statutorily entitled. The taxpayers' alleged injury was not a direct result of the enforcement of the education funding statute, or fairly traceable to defendants' actions in enacting the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Jackson v. Bd. of Election Comm'rs


Docket No. 111928


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


975 N.E.2d 583; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 995; 2012 IL 111928; 363 Ill. Dec. 557



September 7, 2012, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Jackson v. Bd. of Election Comm'rs, 407 Ill. App. 3d 837, 944 N.E.2d 439, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 104, 348 Ill. Dec. 486 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2011)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court reversed the trial court's decision that had affirmed defendant Election Board's decision finding appellant candidate was not disqualified from seeking election to a city council based on property taxes owed to the county treasurer and denying the objection of appellee objector to the candidate's nomination papers. The state supreme court granted the candidate's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The objector filed an objection to the candidate seeking election to the city council in an upcoming election based on homestead exemptions on property owned by the candidate and her husband that were challenged. The couple subsequently elected to waive the exemptions and pay the county treasurer the additional property tax owed. The Election Board ruled that she was not disqualified and denied the objection to her nomination papers. The trial court upheld the Election Board's decision, but the appellate court reversed, set aside the Election Board's decision, and ordered that if her name could not be removed from the ballot, any votes cast for her would not be counted. The state supreme court found that the controversy was moot because the election had already occurred, but determined that the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine applied because public officials needed guidance on the matter. It then found that she could not be disqualified under the Municipal Code, 65 ILCS 5/3.1-10-5(b) (2010), for being in arrears in the payment of a tax or other indebtedness due to a municipality since the tax she owed was owed to the county, rather than a municipality.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment.
