Santiago v. E.W. Bliss Co.


Docket No. 111792


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


973 N.E.2d 858; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 992; 2012 IL 111792; 362 Ill. Dec. 462



August 9, 2012, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Leave to appeal, Appellate Court, First District. (1-10-0780, 1-10-0796).
Santiago v. E.W. Bliss Co., 406 Ill. App. 3d 449, 941 N.E.2d 275, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1379, 346 Ill. Dec. 717 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court, in a product liability action, held: (1) a trial court had discretion to dismiss plaintiff injured man's cause of action with prejudice as a sanction for filing a complaint with a fictitious name and without leave of court and (2) it had to dismiss his cause of action with prejudice because his amended complaint did not relate back to the initial filing. The state supreme court granted his request to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The injured man was badly hurt while using a punch press for the employer. He timely filed a product liability complaint against defendant manufacturers, who had made press parts. The complaint identified him by a first and last name he commonly used. Later, in a deposition, he stated his real first and last name. The trial court denied the manufacturers' motion to dismiss attacking use of the fictitious name, and the filing of his second amended complaint using his real name on the ground that it did not relate back to the timely filed complaint. The trial court then certified the question of whether he could be sanctioned for filing using a fictitious name without leave of court pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-401(e) (2008) and whether the second amended complaint could relate back under 735 ILCS 5/2-616(b) (2008). The appellate court answered affirmatively to the first issue, with qualifications, and affirmatively as to the second issue. The state supreme court found as to the first issue, dismissal was within the trial court's discretion. It found as to the second issue that the original complaint was not per se a nullity and the second amended complaint could relate back.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed that part of the appellate court's judgment that held the trial court had to dismiss an injured plaintiff's product liability action with prejudice under the relation back doctrine. Otherwise, it ordered that the trial court's judgment be vacated and the case be remanded to the trial court to conduct a new hearing to determine whether dismissal as a sanction was required under the standards it set forth.

People v. Hollins


Docket No. 112754


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


971 N.E.2d 504; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 988; 2012 IL 112754; 361 Ill. Dec. 402



June 21, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hollins v. Illinois, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8567 (U.S., Nov. 5, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Hollins, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1546 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction, entered following a stipulated bench trial, finding defendant guilty of child pornography pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(i) (2008), 720 ILCS 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(ii) (2008), and 720 ILCS 5/11-20.1(a)(4) (2008), after he challenged the constitutionality of the child pornography statute as applied to him. The state supreme court granted his petition for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted following a stipulated bench trial of three counts of child pornography pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(i) (2008), 720 ILCS 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(ii) (2008), 720 ILCS 5/11-20.1(a)(4) (2008). On appeal, he challenged the constitutionality of that statute as applied to him, especially since the 17-year-old victim pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/12-16(d) (2008) could legally consent to the sex act itself, but he was prosecuted for recording it with a cell phone camera. The appellate court affirmed. It also found, as to his equal protection challenge, that since no fundamental right nor suspect class was involved, rational basis review allowed the convictions to be upheld because the statutes were rationally related to a legitimate government purpose, and were neither arbitrary nor discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, which had upheld defendant's convictions following a stipulated bench trial.

People v. Clemons


(Docket No. 107821)


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


968 N.E.2d 1046; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 341; 2012 IL 107821; 360 Ill. Dec. 293



April 19, 2012, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
People v. Clemons, 385 Ill. App. 3d 1147, 970 N.E.2d 136, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 5346, 361 Ill. Dec. 136 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Nov. 26, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery while armed with a firearm and home invasion while armed with a firearm. The Illinois Appellate Court held that the matter must be remanded for resentencing. The State's petition for leave to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in 2006. Each offense was a Class X felony, which carried a sentence of 6 to 30 years' imprisonment, plus a 15-year sentencing enhancement for use of a firearm. Thus, the sentencing range was 21 to 45 years. The trial court sentenced defendant to a term of 25 years' imprisonment for each offense, to be served concurrently. The appellate court held that because defendant was sentenced under a statute which violated the proportionate penalties clause, the matter must be remanded for resentencing, and on remand defendant would be subject to a term of 6 to 30 years' imprisonment for his armed robbery conviction, rather than a term of 21 to 45 years' imprisonment. The State argued that the Hauschild decision should be overruled because it misconstrued the armed violence statute and misapplied the identical elements test. The reviewing court held that Hauschild remained the law as to the meaning of the armed violence statute prior to its amendment by 2007 Ill. Laws 95-688.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Wilson v. County of Cook


Docket No. 112026


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2012 IL 112026; 968 N.E.2d 641; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 337; 360 Ill. Dec. 148



April 5, 2012, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Wilson v. Cook County, 407 Ill. App. 3d 759, 943 N.E.2d 768, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 77, 348 Ill. Dec. 160 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff challengers' complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief as to the constitutionality of defendant county's ordinance banning assault weapons. They had alleged that it violated due process rights due to vagueness, equal protection, and the Second Amendment right to bear arms. The state supreme court granted their petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The challengers filed a preenforcement action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against the county and defendant county officials that challenged the constitutionality of a county ordinance known as the Blair Holt Assault Weapons Ban. They claimed, inter alia, that it violated due process on vagueness grounds, as well as the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and the Second Amendment right to bear arms. The trial court dismissed the first amended complaint, pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2006), upon finding that the challengers failed to state a cause of action. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court agreed with the trial and appellate courts about the dismissal of the due process and equal protection claims after it found that vagueness did not permeate the law's text, its prohibitions were clearly defined, and the ordinance did not arbitrarily differentiate between two owners with similar firearms. However, it did find that dismissal as to the Second Amendment claim was improper because it was not clear that assault weapons ran afoul of it, and the county also needed an opportunity to present evidence in favor of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's dismissal of the first-amended complaint as to the due process and equal protection challenges. However, it reversed the appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's dismissal as to the Second Amendment challenge, and remanded the case to the trial court four further proceedings.

People v. Washington


Docket No. 107993


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2012 IL 107993; 969 N.E.2d 349; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 314; 360 Ill. Dec. 539



February 17, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Washington, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 681 (Ill., May 29, 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wash. v. Ill., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8449 (U.S., Oct. 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Washington, 386 Ill. App. 3d 1120, 970 N.E.2d 624, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 4981, 361 Ill. Dec. 258 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment of the Appellate Court of Illinois finding that the evidence was insufficient to uphold defendant's convictions for armed robbery (720 ILCS 5/18-2 (2000)), aggravated kidnapping (720 ILCS 5/10-2 (2000)) and aggravated vehicular hijacking (720 ILCS 5/18-4 (2000)). Defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court remanded the cause to the circuit court with instructions that judgment and sentences be entered on lesser-included offenses (kidnapping, vehicular hijacking, and robbery). The State claimed the appellate court erred when it relied on People v. Ross to reverse the convictions. The supreme court agreed. Given the victim's unequivocal testimony and the circumstances under which he was able to view a gun, the jury could have reasonably inferred that defendant possessed a real gun. Viewing the evidence in a light most favorable to the State, the jurors, as the triers of fact, could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was armed with a dangerous weapon when he committed the offenses of kidnapping, vehicular hijacking and robbery. Defendant claimed the allegations in his indictment varied from the State's proof at trial with regard to the type of dangerous weapon used. However, because the indictment charged him with committing the offenses while armed with a dangerous weapon, "to wit: a firearm," defendant was fully apprised of the charges lodged against him. There was no variance, fatal or otherwise, between the indictment and the proof at trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping and aggravated vehicular hijacking were affirmed. The appellate court judgment which reduced defendant's convictions to their lesser-included offenses was reversed.

Innovative Modular Solutions v. Hazel Crest Sch. Dist. 152.5, 407 Ill. App. 3d 143, 943 N.E.2d 283, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 76, 347 Ill. Dec. 993 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2011)

Sandholm v. Kuecker


Docket No. 111443


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


962 N.E.2d 418; 2012 Ill. LEXIS 33; 2012 IL 111443; 356 Ill. Dec. 733; 40 Media L. Rep. 1209



January 20, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 21, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Sandholm v. Kuecker, 405 Ill. App. 3d 835, 942 N.E.2d 544, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1095, 347 Ill. Dec. 341 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a high school basketball coach, challenged a judgment from the appellate court (Illinois), which affirmed the circuit court's dismissal pursuant to the Citizen Participation Act, 735 ILCS 110/1 et seq. (2008), of defamation and other tort claims against defendants, individuals who had petitioned the school board to remove the coach and local media that had published their criticisms. The circuit court awarded statutory attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The petition to remove the coach asserted that he had been abusive toward players. The school board considered the petition and initially voted to retain the coach, but it removed him after further criticisms were published in the local media. The court noted that the motions to dismiss should have been filed under 735 ILCS 5/2-619(a)(9) (2008), rather than 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2008), and treated them as if they had been so filed. After considering the public policy expressed in 735 ILCS 110/5 (2008), the court concluded that the coach's lawsuit was not a SLAPP under the definitions in 735 ILCS 110/10 (2008), 110/15 (2008) because the lawsuit was not solely based on, related to, or in response to acts in furtherance of the rights of petition and speech. The coach sought to recover damages for personal harm to his reputation, not to stifle political expression. Thus, the burden of proof never shifted to the coach under 735 ILCS 110/20(c) (2008). Although that ruling made the attorney fees issue moot, the court addressed the issue under the public interest exception and interpreted 735 ILCS 110/25 (2008) to include only those fees specifically incurred in connection with the motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the appellate court and the circuit court. The court remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

People v. One 1998 GMC


Docket No. 110236


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2011 IL 110236; 960 N.E.2d 1071; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 2238; 355 Ill. Dec. 900



December 30, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by One 1998 GMC v. Illinois, 132 S. Ct. 2718, 183 L. Ed. 2d 68, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 4274 (U.S., June 4, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. One 1998 GMC, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 2233 (Ill., Dec. 30, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An Illinois trial court dismissed three forfeiture complaints with prejudice that the State had filed against appellees after finding that the statutory forfeiture provisions, 720 ILCS 5/36-1 through 36-4 (2006), were facially unconstitutional. The trial court denied the State's motion to reconsider. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the vehicle-forfeiture provisions of 720 ILCS 5/36-1 through 36-4 (2006) were not facially unconstitutional as a violation of procedural due process under the Fifth and 14th Amendments and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, even though they did not include a provision requiring a prompt, probable cause hearing after the seizure of a vehicle, because the forfeiture proceeding itself provided all the process that was due. Applying the Baker factors pursuant to United States Supreme Court precedent, the court found that: (1) the State filed its complaints for forfeiture within 22, 20, and 20 days of each of the seizures pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/36-2(a) (2006); (2) it did not appear that the claimants took any steps to obtain an early return of their vehicles but rather filed several motions for continuances before waiting several months to file a motion to dismiss; and (3) the claimants did not allege any undue delay, let alone prejudice from the delay.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Hammond


Docket Nos. 110044, 110705 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


959 N.E.2d 29; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1839; 2011 IL 110044; 355 Ill. Dec. 1



December 1, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.

Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Hammond, 397 Ill. App. 3d 342, 925 N.E.2d 1185, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1388, 339 Ill. Dec. 64 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: One Illinois Appellate Court rejected defendant's argument that probation officers lacked the power to file petitions alleging a probation violation and seeking probation revocation. A second Illinois Appellate Court rejected the State's claim that 730 ILCS 5/5-6-4(i) (2006) unduly infringed on the executive branch or, more specifically, the State's Attorneys in prosecuting probation violations. Defendant and the State, respectively, appealed.


OVERVIEW: In one case, defendant's probation officer indicated to the trial court that defendant was violating his probation. Defendant unsuccessfully claimed on appeal that only the State's Attorney had the power to seek probation revocation. In a second, separate case, the trial court could impose intermediate sanctions in lieu of revoking probation, and though each of three defendants accepted and completed a program of intermediate sanctions, the State's Attorney nevertheless sought probation revocation. The three defendants successfully sought dismissal of the revocation petitions. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court consolidated the appeals. It then found that probation officers, pursuant to 730 ILCS 5/5-6-4(i) (2006), had the power to file petitions alleging violations of probation with the trial court, as occurred regarding defendant in the first case. It also found that the State's Attorney could not veto a probation officer's offer of intermediate sanctions, as long as the sanctions were timely completed, and such a finding did not violate the separation of powers doctrine because the ultimate authority regarding probation violations was in the judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgments.

People v. Villa


Docket No. 110777


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


959 N.E.2d 634; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1832; 2011 IL 110777; 355 Ill. Dec. 220



December 1, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Villa, 403 Ill. App. 3d 309, 932 N.E.2d 90, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 684, 342 Ill. Dec. 199 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed defendant's conviction entered after a jury found guilty of aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated discharge of a firearm under an accountability theory, stemming from a drive-by shooting, and after he had been sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 14 years and five years, respectively. The state supreme court granted defendant's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's friend was attacked, defendant accompanied his friend to where the attackers were located. The friend then fired shots, which injured one of them. Defendant was charged with aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated discharge of a firearm under an accountability theory. Prior to trial, he moved in limine to prohibit the State from introducing evidence regarding his juvenile adjudication for burglary, which had occurred less than a year before the shooting. The trial court denied the motion in limine, and the State referred to the adjudication at least twice in closing argument. Defendant was convicted of both charges. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court found that the main issue before it was whether reversible error occurred when the State was allowed to impeach defendant, who testified at trial, with his prior juvenile adjudication for burglary. The state supreme court found that: (1) pursuant to 705 ILCS 405/5-150(1)(c) (2006), a juvenile adjudication was typically not admissible against a testifying defendant; (2) defendant did not "open the door" to the admission of such evidence; and (3) the error in admitting it was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for it to conduct a new trial.

 

86 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Crossroads Ford Truck Sales v. Sterling Truck Corp.


Docket No. 111611


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


959 N.E.2d 1133; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1837; 2011 IL 111611; 355 Ill. Dec. 400



December 1, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
Crossroads Ford Truck Sales, Inc. v. Sterling Truck Corp., 406 Ill. App. 3d 325, 943 N.E.2d 646, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1268, 348 Ill. Dec. 38 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motor vehicle dealer filed a complaint against defendants, truck manufacturers and a chief executive officer, alleging violations of the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act (the Act), 815 ILCS 710/1 et seq. (2010), and claims of breach of contract, tortious interference with contract, and fraud. The circuit court dismissed all but two counts with prejudice. The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed. The dealer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court properly held that the circuit court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear several counts and portions of counts brought under § 4(d)(6) of the Act, 815 ILCS 710/4(d)(6), because those counts should have been brought before the Motor Vehicle Review Board (MVRB). The circuit court was not authorized to determine good cause in conjunction with § 4(d)(6) because good cause determinations under § 4(d)(6) had to be made by the MVRB. The legislature intended to deprive the circuit courts of jurisdiction to make good cause determinations and thus no concurrent jurisdiction existed. Accordingly, primary jurisdiction was not applicable. Without concurrent or original jurisdiction, there was no primary jurisdiction. The case could not have been brought originally in the circuit court and then referred out by that court because that court had no jurisdiction over the subject matter in the first place. The two-step process of first obtaining a good cause finding from the MVRB and then seeking damages from the circuit court did not run afoul of the doctrine of res judicata because the MVRB was not empowered to award damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Forest Preserve Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank


Docket Nos. 110759, 110760 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


961 N.E.2d 775; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1840; 2011 IL 110759; 356 Ill. Dec. 386



December 1, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 21, 2012.
Rehearing denied by Forest Pres. Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 37 (Ill., Jan. 23, 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Forest Pres. Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 7575 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Forest Preserve Dist. of Du Page County v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park, 401 Ill. App. 3d 966, 930 N.E.2d 477, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 501, 341 Ill. Dec. 267 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Appellate court judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condemnor filed an action against defendant condemnees under the Eminent Domain Act, 735 ILCS 5/7-101 et seq. (1998). The trial court enter judgment on the jury's award determining the fair market value of the property. The Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District, affirmed in part, but vacated the jury's verdict as to the value of the property. Both the condemnor and the Attorney General appealed.


OVERVIEW: The condemnor notified the condemnees that it intended to acquire the property, offered to pay a certain sum, and gave the condemnees time to respond. The condemnees rejected the initial offer. The trial court granted summary judgment to the condemnor on acting-in-good-faith and motion in limine issues, and declined the condemnees' Kirby motion for a post-hearing valuation. The condemnees did not forfeit their right to have just compensation valued using a point in time other than the date of the filing of the action in accordance with 735 ILCS 5/7-121 (1998) because they raised the constitutionality of the statute as applied at the hearing on the Kirby motion one month before trial. As to the merits of the argument, a taking did not occur until, at the very earliest, the date the government deposited the condemnation award and was given the right to take title and possession. Also, the appellate court properly determined that the condemnnees were not required to file a demand for a speedy trial, and that the condemnor still had the option to abandon the proceeding if it chose to do so. Finally, the record indicated that the condemnor negotiated in good faith as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

A.B.A.T.E. of Ill. v. Quinn


Docket No. 110611


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


957 N.E.2d 876; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1825; 2011 IL 110611; 354 Ill. Dec. 282



October 27, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: A.B.A.T.E. of Ill., Inc. v. Giannoulias, 401 Ill. App. 3d 326, 929 N.E.2d 1188, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 498, 341 Ill. Dec. 109 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court held that the removal of funds from the Cycle Rider Safety Training Fund (CRSTF) was not an unconstitutional taking, and that the legislature had the authority to order a transfer of funds out of the CRSTF and into the General Revenue Fund. The state supreme court granted plaintiff objectors' petition for leave to appeal to it.


OVERVIEW: The legislature amended the Cycle Rider Safety Training Act, 625 ILCS 35/1 et seq. (1994), to change the Cycle Rider Safety Training Fund (CRSTF) from a special fund inside the state treasury to a "trust fund outside of the State treasury," as set forth in 625 ILCS 35/6 (1994). The legislature also authorized the transfer of money from that fund into the State's General Revenue Fund, through budget implementation acts and State Finance Act amendments. Eventually, the objectors sued to challenge transfers made from the CRSTF and into the General Revenue Fund. Primarily, they alleged that such conduct by defendant state officials was an unconstitutional taking of private property. The trial court disagreed and granted summary judgment to the state officials. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court found that the amendment changing the CRSTF did not make what were public funds private funds. It also found the legislature could not create an irrevocable trust with the public funds because it did not have the authority to bind subsequent legislatures, and that transferring the funds involved permissibly removing property in one trust and placing it in another state fund.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

Wirtz v. Quinn


Docket No. 111903


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


953 N.E.2d 899; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1107; 2011 IL 111903; 352 Ill. Dec. 218



July 11, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Wirtz v. Quinn, 407 Ill. App. 3d 776, 942 N.E.2d 765, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 33, 347 Ill. Dec. 562 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, petitioner on behalf of all taxpayers, challenged the judgment of the Illinois Appellate Court, finding that 2009 Ill. Laws 34 violated the single subject clause of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d), and that 2009 Ill. Laws 35, 37 and 39 were invalid based on language making their enactment contingent on the enactment of 2009 Ill. Laws 34.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that the four Public Acts violated various provisions of the Illinois Constitution, and the circuit court denied the plaintiffs' petition. The appellate court reversed, finding that 2009 Ill. Laws 34 violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution, because the provisions did not have a natural and logical connection to the single subject of revenue. The appellate court also held that 2009 Ill. Laws 35, 37 and 38 could not stand because they were expressly contingent on the enactment of 2009 Ill. Laws 34. The reviewing court held that 2009 Ill. Laws 34 was a constitutionally legitimate enactment genuinely encompassing one subject, and there was no single subject violation in 2009 Ill. Laws 37 or 38. Also, the contingency provisions in 2009 Ill. Laws 34, 35, 37, and 38 clearly were reasonably related to one another in that they were associated with raising funds for capital projects, establishing capital projects, and appropriating funds to those projects. Furthermore, there was no violation of the Presentment Clause, the Effective Date of Laws Clause, veto procedures, the separation of powers, the Public Funds Clause, or the Uniformity Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Jonathon C.B. (In re Jonathon C.B.)


Docket No. 107750


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2011 IL 107750; 958 N.E.2d 227; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1102; 354 Ill. Dec. 484



June 30, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected November 28, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. Jonathon C.B. (In re Jonathon C.B.), 2011 IL 107750, 958 N.E.2d 227, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 2231, 354 Ill. Dec. 484 (2011)
Rehearing denied by People v. Jonathon C.B. (In re Jonathon C.B.), 2011 Ill. LEXIS 2241 (Ill., Nov. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
People v. Jonathan C.B. (In re Jonathan C.B.), 386 Ill. App. 3d 735, 898 N.E.2d 252, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1172, 325 Ill. Dec. 519 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2008)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals of Illinois that affirmed a circuit court's adjudication of delinquency based upon a finding that the juvenile was guilty of criminal sexual assault in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-13(a)(1) (2006) and attempted robbery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/8-4(a) and 18-1 (2006), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support the ajudication.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that, despite the inconsistencies concerning events collateral to the criminal sexual conduct, the testimony of the victim and the other witnesses was consistent concerning the sexual assault. The victim testified that the juvenile's brother grabbed her and pulled her behind a duplex, pushed her down, and crammed his penis into her mouth, telling her not to bite. The juvenile then inserted his penis into her vagina from behind. The victim reported to the police and a paramedic that she had been raped, and both witnesses described the victim as emotional and hysterical. A deputy testified that the victim's shirt and bra strap were torn and that she had abrasions on her elbows and arms. In contrast, the juvenile's statements concerning the sexual encounter were inconsistent, initially denying any sexual contact when confronted by police and later indicating that he paid the victim for sex and that the sexual encounter was consensual. It was for the trier of fact to resolve conflicts in the testimony, and the evidence, taken together, was sufficient to satisfy the trial court beyond a reasonable doubt of the juvenile's guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

Clark v. Children's Mem. Hosp.


Docket No. 108656


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


955 N.E.2d 1065; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 772; 2011 IL 108656; 353 Ill. Dec. 254



May 6, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 27, 2011. As Corrected December 14, 2011.
Reported at Clark v. Children's Mem. Hosp., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 773 (Ill., May 6, 2011)
Rehearing denied by Clark v. Children's Mem. Hosp., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1261 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas L. Hogan, Judge, presiding.
Clark v. Children's Mem. Hosp., 391 Ill. App. 3d 321, 907 N.E.2d 49, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 222, 329 Ill. Dec. 730 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant health care providers appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals of Illinois that held that plaintiff parents in a wrongful birth case could recover damages for the cost of caring for their dependent, disabled adult child and further held that the parents adequately pled a cause of action for negligent infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed suit against the health care providers, alleging that the health care providers failed to advise them of the results of genetic testing done on their first child and that, had they been properly advised, they would not have conceived a second child. On review, the court held that, in Illinois, parents had no obligation to support a disabled child beyond the age of majority. Because the parents had no duty to provide post-majority support, such expenses were not legal harms suffered by the parents and were not compensable damages in a wrongful birth action. Further, the court overruled its prior ruling in Siemieniec v. Lutheran General Hospital, 117 Ill. 2d 230 (1987), which applied the zone of danger rule to wrongful birth plaintiffs' claims for emotional distress. The zone of danger rule applied only in cases where the theory of liability was the negligent infliction of emotional distress; it did not apply where, as in a wrongful birth case, a tort had already been committed against the parents and they asserted emotional distress as an element of damages for that tort.


OUTCOME: That portion of the appellate court's judgment reversing the circuit court's dismissal of the parents' claim for negligent infliction of emotional distress was affirmed, but that portion of the appellate court judgment holding that the parents were entitled to recover damages for the post-majority expenses of caring for their son was reversed. The case was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Goodman v. Ward


Docket No. 109796.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


241 Ill. 2d 398; 948 N.E.2d 580; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 446; 350 Ill. Dec. 300



March 24, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District.
Goodman v. Ward, 397 Ill. App. 3d 875, 922 N.E.2d 522, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 24, 337 Ill. Dec. 399 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed a trial court's judgment in holding that the name of a nonresident candidate for trial court judge in a judicial subcircuit should not appear on an official ballot for an upcoming primary election if he or she was not a resident of the subcircuit when he or she submitted a nomination petition to the office. The state supreme court granted appellant nonresident candidate's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The nonresident candidate submitted nominating papers for a primary election for the office of trial judge of a particular judicial subcircuit that stated he was a resident of the subcircuit. Appellee registered voter objected that the nonresident candidate was not eligible for the office because he did not actually reside in the subcircuit, but the Board found that residency was not required at the time the nominating papers were filed and denied the objection. The trial court reversed that decision. The appellate court affirmed the reversal. The state supreme court rejected the nonresident's claim that he only had to be a resident of the subcircuit at the time he took the office rather than before that time. It found that under the plain language of 10 ILCS 5/7-10 (2008), he had to be qualified for the office of trial judge at the time he filed his nomination papers and being qualified pursuant to that statute meant he also had to be a resident of the relevant subcircuit at that time, as dictated by Ill. Const. art. VI, § 11, which he had conceded he was not.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, which had affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Madrigal


Docket No. 110194.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


241 Ill. 2d 463; 948 N.E.2d 591; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 454; 350 Ill. Dec. 311



March 24, 2011, Opinion Filed


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted dismissal to defendant, who had been on one count of identity theft in violation of of the Identity Theft Law, 720 ILCS 5/16G-15(a)(7) (2008), after defendant claimed that the statute failed to require a culpable mental state and, thus, could be applied to wholly-innocent conduct in violation of her due process rights. The State appealed to the state supreme court as a matter of right.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for identity theft in violation of the Identity Theft Law, 720 ILCS 5/16G-15(a)(7) (2008). That law provided that a person committed that offense by knowingly using any personal identification information or personal identification document of another to gain access to any record of the actions taken, communications made or received, or other activities or transactions of that person, without the prior express permission of that person. The indictment alleged that defendant knowingly used personal identification information of a specific person without the prior express permission of that person. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss on the ground that the specific statutory provision under which she was indicted did not contain a culpable mental state and, thus, violated her right to due process. The state supreme court found that the statutory provision in question violated her substantive due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 because its mental state of knowledge, without a culpable mental state, allowed it to punish conduct that had no criminal purpose.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Hill v. Walker


Docket No. 110215.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


241 Ill. 2d 479; 948 N.E.2d 601; 2011 Ill. LEXIS 452; 350 Ill. Dec. 321



March 24, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
Hill v. Walker, 397 Ill. App. 3d 1090, 924 N.E.2d 554, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 147, 338 Ill. Dec. 348 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court entered a judgment that affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff inmate's action seeking declaratory and mandamus relief against defendants, a corrections director and a prisoner review board, after the Board denied his motion recent request for release on parole in a case where he had been convicted of murdering two people. The state supreme court granted the inmate's pro se petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two murders. He was finally sentenced to two concurrent terms of 30 to 90 years. His requests for parole were denied several times. Also, changes in statutory law permitted annual parole hearings to occur as far apart as every three years. Eventually, he filed a second-amended complaint seeking declaratory and mandamus relief from the parole release denials and claimed that the Illinois parole process violated his constitutional rights. The trial court dismissed that complaint. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court found that following a conviction and sentencing, the Illinois parole release statute did not give an inmate a legitimate expectation of parole that became a liberty interest protected by procedural due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, especially given the Board's discretion in granting parole. It also found the Illinois parole release statute was not an ex post facto law in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 since it did not extend punishment and changes in the Board's interpretation of the criteria for parole was not an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed the trial court's summary dismissal of defendant's pro se postconviction relief petition in a case where he was convicted of first-degree murder after a bench trial. It then modified fees and costs the trial court imposed after entering the summary dismissal. The state supreme court granted his petition for leave to appeal challenging the constitutionality of the statute used to impose the fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder following a bench trial. Thereafter, he filed a pro se postconviction relief petition pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/122-2.1 (2006). The trial court summarily dismissed his pro se postconviction petition, finding that he failed to raise the claims in his direct appeal and that res judicata prevented consideration of them. Indeed, it concluded his postconviction claims were frivolous and patently without merit. Due to the summary dismissal, the trial court imposed fees and costs upon him pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/22-105 (2006) regarding frivolous prisoner pleadings. The appellate court affirmed after modifying the fees and costs. The state supreme court determined that the term frivolous meant the same thing in 735 ILCS 5/22-105(b)(1) (2006) as it did in 725 ILCS 5/122-2.1 (2006) of the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. It then found that 735 ILCS 5/22-105 (2006) did not violate his due process rights since he did not have a fundamental right to file frivolous pleadings and did not violate his equal protection rights because prisoners were not a suspect class and that statute furthered the legislature's goal on reducing frivolous prisoner pleadings.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

People v. Baez

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a direct appeal to the court from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 603, defendant, who had pleaded guilty to two murders and had been sentenced to death, challenged his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the removal of his counsel violated his Sixth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 8 (1970) right to counsel. The trial court removed counsel after learning that he was not ready to provide representation to defendant. The appeals court found counsel did not and likely could not tell the court when he would return from vacation in Israel. Counsel's request that another attorney be appointed while counsel was gone undermined counsel's claim that he was ready, willing, and able to represent defendant. Defendant's capital sentence was found to be proper pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/9-1 (2008), as he coldly and brutally murdered two persons who had done nothing to him. While his abusive childhood and early introduction to drugs were mitigating indications of his troubled past, he had rejected multiple attempts to provide the help he needed to overcome that past. The trial court did not erroneously reject the mitigating factor of extreme mental or emotional disturbance. Contrary to defendant's assertion that he lacked emotional control, he explained to officers that he chose to kill a victim because if the victim lived he would have defendant killed.

People v. Stoffel


Docket No. 108500


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


239 Ill. 2d 314; 941 N.E.2d 147; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1896; 346 Ill. Dec. 589



December 23, 2010, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
People v. Stoffel, 389 Ill. App. 3d 238, 907 N.E.2d 79, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 217, 329 Ill. Dec. 760 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed as modified; circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court held that a trial court's decision to not to "recharacterize" a pleading filed by a pro se defendant as a postconviction petition may be reviewed for error. Consequently, it reversed a judgment that dismissed defendant's pro se pleading, and remanded defendant's case with instructions to recharacterize the pleading as a postconviction petition. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of unlawful manufacture of a substance containing methamphetamine weighing between 400 and 900 grams, in violation of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, 720 ILCS 570/401(a)(6.5)(C) (2004). He filed a "petition for relief from judgment," pursuant to the Illinois and federal constitutions, and 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2006). He contended that the waste product was not intended to be considered part of the substance containing methamphetamine, and including it resulted in an unconstitutional penalty. The trial court took actions that indicated that it was recharacterizing the petition as a 725 ILCS 5/122-1(d) (2006) postconviction relief petition, but it then dismissed the petition anyway. The appellate court viewed the trial court's decision as a refusal to recharacterize the petition and reversed the dismissal. The state supreme court found that the trial court was not obligated to recharacterize the petition, but having done so, it should not have dismissed the petition. However, it also found on the merits that the legislature had not intended to exclude the weight of waste products from the drug weight for sentencing purposes.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed that part of the appellate court's judgment which reversed the judgment of dismissal entered by the trial court. It then modified the appellate court's remand instructions so as to direct the trial court to enter an order allowing defense counsel's amendments to defendant's postconviction petition and to deny defendant's postconviction petition on the merits.

101 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ligon


Docket No. 108855


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


239 Ill. 2d 94; 940 N.E.2d 1067; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1560; 346 Ill. Dec. 463



November 18, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended January 25, 2011.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ligon v. Ill., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 2193 (U.S., Mar. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Ligon, 392 Ill. App. 3d 988, 910 N.E.2d 1252, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 531, 331 Ill. Dec. 496 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for postconviction relief from his conviction of aggravated vehicular hijacking under 720 ILCS 5/18-4(a)(3) (2002) and life sentence, which was denied. The Court of Appeals of Illinois affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that dismissal of defendant's postconviction petition did not violate the equal protection and due process clauses of the federal constitution because: (1) there was no federal constitutional right to the assistance of counsel connected with proceedings seeking collateral relief, even where those proceedings were the first tier of review of an ineffective assistance of counsel claim; (2) defendant was well-equipped to present his claims on collateral review, given the numerous documents in his possession prepared by appellate counsel addressing his ineffective assistance of counsel claims; and (3) there was no obstacle to a review of defendant's conviction on direct appeal, and defendant merely had to allege his ineffective assistance claim in his postconviction petition to receive the appointment of counsel. Because he did not do so, as advised to do so by an appellate court on direct appeal, he could not now raise the claims in his postconviction petition, and it was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendant postconviction relief was affirmed.

People v. Dabbs


Docket No. 109698


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


239 Ill. 2d 277; 940 N.E.2d 1088; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1555; 346 Ill. Dec. 484



November 18, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dabbs v. Illinois, 131 S. Ct. 2158, 179 L. Ed. 2d 942, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 3337 (U.S., 2011)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Dabbs v. Taylor, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 70814 (S.D. Ill., May 22, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District.
People v. Dabbs, 396 Ill. App. 3d 622, 919 N.E.2d 501, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1236, 335 Ill. Dec. 782 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant after a jury found him guilty of domestic battery against his girlfriend. He had argued on appeal that permitting his ex-wife to testify pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (2008) was error because that statute was unconstitutional. The state supreme court granted defendant's petition for leave to appeal to review the appellate court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: The alleged victim went to a police station to report that she had been battered by defendant, her then-boyfriend. She reported to the police officer who interviewed her that defendant had struck and threatened to kill her. The officer observed that she had a black eye and bruises on her arms. Defendant was arrested and charged with, inter alia, domestic battery of her. Prior to trial, the State moved to admit evidence of a prior incident of domestic violence committed by defendant against his ex-wife, as permitted under 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (2008) regarding admission of evidence of prior acts of domestic violence. The trial court eventually granted the motion. Following a trial at which his ex-wife testified about defendant striking her, he was convicted of domestic battery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2006). The appellate court, in affirming, rejected his claim that 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (Supp. 2007) violated his right to due process. The state supreme court found that the statute was constitutional because it allowed admission of "other acts" evidence if the requirements of the statute were met and other applicable evidence rules, such as relevance, were followed.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

103 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Wright Dev. Group, LLC v. Walsh


Docket No. 109463


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


238 Ill. 2d 620; 939 N.E.2d 389; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1537; 345 Ill. Dec. 546



October 21, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 19, 2010. Counsel Amended December 23, 2010.
Appeal after remand at, Appeal dismissed by Wright Dev. Group, LLC v. Walsh, 2014 IL App (1st) 130646-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1583 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Wright Dev. Group, LLC v. Walsh, 393 Ill. App. 3d 1107, 985 N.E.2d 726, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 4412, 368 Ill. Dec. 919 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee limited liability company sued appellant condominium association president for defamation. In the instant appeal, the court was asked if the president's statement to a reporter during a public forum inside an alderman's office was immunized from the lawsuit under the Citizen Participation Act, 735 ILCS 110/1 et seq. (2008). The trial court found the statement was not immune from suit. The appellate court dismissed the appeal as moot.


OVERVIEW: The president argued that the appellate court's dismissal of the appeal as moot should have been reversed because the legislature clearly intended for the Act to provide an independent and substantive right to appellate review of final trial court orders denying a motion to dispose of a lawsuit brought pursuant to the Citizen Participation Act, 735 ILCS 110/1 et seq. (2008). The court found that the appellate court's failure to undertake the question of whether the limited liability company's lawsuit could be identified as a Strategic Lawsuit Against Public Participation (SLAPP) directly contradicted the legislature's explicit expression of public policy regarding the efficient process to identify and adjudicate SLAPPs. The mootness finding also contradicted the legislature's express finding of public policy in favor of an award attorney fees and costs to prevailing movants. 735 ILCS 110/5 (2008). Further, there was a potential injury to the president because the president was denied the relief requested in his motion under the Act to identify the LLC's lawsuit as a SLAPP and for a statutory award of attorney fees and costs. Accordingly, the president's appeal was not moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court and the trial court orders entered on July 29, 2008, and August 19, 2008 were reversed. The president enjoyed immunity from liability in the lawsuit under the Citizen Participation Act. The case was remanded to the circuit court to award the president reasonable attorney fees and costs incurred in connection with the motion.

Hossfeld v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


Docket No. 109725.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant objector's petition to challenge appellee candidate's eligibility to be a candidate in a primary election for the office of state senator. The state supreme court granted the objector's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The candidate voted a Democratic ballot in a consolidated primary election that occurred in a township. Approximately two months later, the general township election was held. Six months after that election, the candidate filed nomination papers seeking the Republican nomination in a particular legislative district for the office of state senator for the general primary election being held approximately one year after the township had held its consolidated primary election. People v. Veronica C. (In re Veronica C.)


Docket No. 108953


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


239 Ill. 2d 134; 940 N.E.2d 1; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1068; 346 Ill. Dec. 1



September 23, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended January 25, 2011.

Modified upon denial of rehearing November 22, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
In re Veronica C., 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 4787 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 23, 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court rejected respondent minor's claims that the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 ILCS 405/5-615(1) (2006), violated constitutional provisions pertaining to equal protection and separation of powers insofar as it prevented a minor from being placed on supervision without the consent of the State. The state supreme court allowed the minor's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the minor violated 720 ILCS 5/12-3(a)(2) (2006) by committing a battery. She was thereafter placed on probation for a one year under certain conditions and subjected to paying certain fees. On appeal, she claimed that 705 ILCS 405/5-615(1) (2006) of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 violated constitutional provisions pertaining to equal protection and separation of powers because it prevented a minor from being placed on supervision without the consent of the State. The appellate court rejected those contentions. The state supreme court found that it did not need to reach the constitutional arguments because 705 ILCS 405/5-615(1) (2006) (Act) did not apply to her. It so concluded because it found that by the time in the trial court proceedings that the trial court asked the State about its position on supervision, supervision was no longer an option under the Act's procedural framework because a finding of delinquency had already been entered; it determined that the possibility of supervision had to be broached and considered, if at all, before proceeding to findings and adjudication had occurred.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

Hubble v. Bi-State Dev. Agency of the Illinois-Missouri Metro. Dist.


Docket No. 109137


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


238 Ill. 2d 262; 938 N.E.2d 483; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1066; 345 Ill. Dec. 44



September 23, 2010, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
Hubble v. Bi-State Dev. Agency, 393 Ill. App. 3d 1016, 915 N.E.2d 64, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 761, 333 Ill. Dec. 543 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court order reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court answered "no" to whether defendant bus operator was a "local public entity" as defined by the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 ILCS 10/1-101 et seq. (2006), and thereby subject to its one-year statute of limitations after the trial court denied plaintiff motorist's motion to dismiss. It then granted a certificate of importance for the state supreme court to review that ruling.


OVERVIEW: A bus owned and operated by the bus operated collided with the motorist's automobile at an intersection in an Illinois city. Approximately 17 months later, the motorist sued the bus operator for alleged personal injuries he sustained. His complaint was filed within the two-year general statute of limitations for personal injury actions, 735 ILCS 5/13-202 (2006), but beyond the one-year statute of limitations, 745 ILCS 10/8-101(a) (2006) for actions against local public entities under the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act). The bus operator moved to dismiss, alleged that the Act's limitations period applied to it, and claimed the motorist's action was untimely. The trial court denied the motion, but certified to the appellate court the question of whether the bus operator was a "local public entity." The appellate court said it was not. The state supreme court disagreed with the trial and appellate courts, and found that bus operator, as a"not-for-profit" corporation, was a "local public entity" under 745 ILCS 10/1-206 (2006) of the Act, and, thus, the Act's one-year statute of limitations applied to bar the motorist's action as untimely.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment, reversed the trial court's order, and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to dismiss the motorist's complaint.

Irwin Indus. Tool Co. v. Ill. Dep't of Revenue


Docket No. 109300


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


238 Ill. 2d 332; 938 N.E.2d 459; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1065; 345 Ill. Dec. 20



September 23, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended November 29, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Irwin Indus. Tool Co. v. Dep't of Revenue, 394 Ill. App. 3d 1002, 915 N.E.2d 789, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 893, 333 Ill. Dec. 718 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of an Illinois appellate court, which affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Illinois Department of Revenue, but reversed the portion of the judgment that had limited the imposition of a use tax upon the taxpayer's purchase of an airplane to only four percent of the airplane value. The Court concluded that Illinois' use tax based on the full purchase price of the airplane was externally consistent and, thus, fairly apportioned because no tax has been paid on the airplane to any other state, and even if it had been, the Use Tax Act provided an exemption for sales or use taxes paid to other states. As a result, the court found that the appellate court properly reversed that portion of the circuit court's judgment limiting the use tax to four percent of the airplane's purchase price.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

108 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hanson


Docket No. 106566.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


238 Ill. 2d 74; 939 N.E.2d 238; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 967; 345 Ill. Dec. 395



June 24, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Hanson, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1074 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Hanson v. Illinois, 131 S. Ct. 2091, 179 L. Ed. 2d 798, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 2822 (U.S., 2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Hanson, 2013 IL App (2d) 111049-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 725 (2013)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of four counts of first degree murder, two counts of armed robbery, two counts of aggravated kidnapping, and two counts of identity theft. Defendant was sentenced to death. The circuit court found that the armed robbery and aggravated kidnapping convictions merged into the murder convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the conviction for aggravated kidnapping was improperly considered by the jury in determining that death was an appropriate sentence. The supreme court disagreed. Facts adduced at trial relating to the aggravated kidnapping charge were not extensive. The State elicited on direct examination from a doctor only that the cause of death of two victims was a gunshot wound to the head. The State did not ask about time of death and did not ask for an opinion on when the victims were moved. Indeed, it was defense counsel who asked the doctor about the time of death. The doctor acknowledged that the victims were immediately brain dead, but that their hearts could have continued beating for seconds or minutes afterward. The State elicited testimony from several witnesses supporting its theory that the victims' bodies had been moved. Thus, the jury was presented with evidence that the victims were shot in their home. The jury was presented with the entire sequence of events, from the shooting to the cleanup to transporting of the victims. The jury was entitled to give those facts and circumstances aggravating weight under the "catch-all" sentencing factor.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for aggravated kidnapping were vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

People v. Boeckmann


Docket Nos. 108289, 108290 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


238 Ill. 2d 1; 932 N.E.2d 998; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 966; 342 Ill. Dec. 537



June 24, 2010, Opinion Filed


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clinton County Circuit Court (Illinois) in two cases declared unconstitutional on due process grounds 625 ILCS 5/6-206(a)(43) (2008) requiring suspension of driving privileges if a person received court supervision for the unlawful consumption of alcohol by a person under the age of 21-years-old. Appellant State, represented by the Secretary, appealed and defendants' appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were each charged with unlawful consumption of alcohol by a person under 21-years-old, in violation of the Liquor Control Act, 235 ILCS 5/6-20(e) (2008). They moved to declare unconstitutional, inter alia, 625 ILCS 5/6-206(a)(43) (2008) of the Vehicle Code. That section generally authorized the Secretary of State (Secretary) to suspend driving privileges upon conviction or disposition of court supervision for the charged offenses. The trial court declared 625 ILCS 5/6-206(a)(43) (2008) unconstitutional on due process grounds as applied. The state supreme court found that since that the statute only had to bear a rational relationship to a legitimate public interest. It then found that it was reasonable for the General Assembly to believe that a young person disobeying the underage drinking law might also drive after drinking. It also found that the Secretary under the statute lacked discretion over whether to suspend their driving privileges and that the suspension did not violate the Illinois Constitution's proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, because it was not a direct action to inflict punishment, but was meant to protect the public.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment that determined the statute at issue regarding suspension of driving privileges was unconstitutional and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Cwik v. Giannoulias


Docket No. 108313.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


237 Ill. 2d 409; 930 N.E.2d 990; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 672; 341 Ill. Dec. 476



May 20, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended July 29, 2010.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cwik v. Giannoulias, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 8116 (U.S., Oct. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Cwik v. Topinka, 389 Ill. App. 3d 21, 905 N.E.2d 300, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 116, 328 Ill. Dec. 766 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court found that while the State's retention of interest earned on property held it pursuant to the Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act, 765 ILCS 1025/15 (2004), might be a taking, it was not a taking for which just compensation was due under the facts of the case, where the property had been abandoned. Plaintiff interest claimants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The interest claimants sued the defendants, the state treasurer and the unclaimed property division director, on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated seeking payment of interest on their property, money in the case of each of the representative plaintiffs, held by the State under the Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act, 765 ILCS 1025/1 et seq. (2004), prior to their claims of reclamation. The trial court certified dispositive questions to the appellate court. The appellate court held that the retention of interest by the State "may" be a "taking" under Ill. Const. art. I, § 15 and the Ffth and Fourteenth Amendments, U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, but because the property owners had abandoned the property, the appellate court concluded it was not a taking for which just compensation was due. The state supreme court found that the legislature could enact a statute divesting the property owners of the right to interest payments, without violating the state or federal constitutions, as it was the neglectful property owners' conduct in abandoning the property rather than any action by the State that caused the loss of the right to the interest payments.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

People v. Johnson

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court entered a judgment that vacated defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated unlawful use of a weapon, and ordered that defendant's case be remanded to the trial court with instructions to amend the sentencing order. The state supreme court granted defendant's petition for leave to appeal.

People v. Averett


Docket Nos. 106362, 106621 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


237 Ill. 2d 1; 927 N.E.2d 1191; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 658; 340 Ill. Dec. 180



April 15, 2010, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Averett, 231 Ill. 2d 671, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 680, 328 Ill. Dec. 471 (2009)
People v. Tucker, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 2557 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 12, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court found that whether trial courts in criminal cases were permitted to apply blanket policies of refusing to rule on motions in limine until after hearing a defendant's testimony was not reviewable because the defendants involved had not testified. It also found that one defendant waived his challenge to the trial court's response to a jury question. The state supreme court granted their petitions for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: In separate cases, one defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver while the second defendant was charged with burglary. In each, the respective defendants filed motions in limine to bar the use of prior convictions for impeachment purposes. In both cases, the one defendant and the second defendant declined to testify. Both defendants were convicted. In the one defendant's case, the trial court in response to a question about clarifying some matters responded that the jury should continue to deliberate. In separate appeals, the appellate court affirmed; it also found the one defendant waived his challenge to the trial court's response involving the jury question. The state supreme court consolidated the appeals. It then found that the respective defendants' challenges were unreviewable because they had not testified in either case. It also held that the one defendant acquiesced in the trial court's response to the jury question by not objecting.

People v. Banks

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


237 Ill. 2d 154; 934 N.E.2d 435; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 272; 343 Ill. Dec. 111

Petition denied by Banks v. Illinois, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 100 (U.S., Jan. 10, 2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury returned a general verdict of guilty of first-degree murder and a verdict of guilty of aggravated discharge of a firearm, stemming from a carjacking. It then sentenced him to death after a jury found him eligible for the death penalty on two statutory grounds. 114 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Lebron v. Gottlieb Mem. Hosp.


Docket Nos. 105741, 105745 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


237 Ill. 2d 217; 930 N.E.2d 895; 2010 Ill. LEXIS 26; 341 Ill. Dec. 381



February 4, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended March 10, 2010. Counsel Amended July 29, 2010.


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), in a medical malpractice and declaratory action filed by the plaintiffs, a minor and her mother, against defendant healthcare providers, found that 735 ILCS 5/2-1706.5 (2008)'s caps on noneconomic damages in medical malpractice cases, both facially and as applied, violated the Ill. Const. art. II, § 1's separation of powers clause. The state supreme court allowed the healthcare providers' direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: The minor and her mother filed a medical malpractice and declaratory judgment action against the healthcare providers alleging that the minor sustained severe permanent injuries due to healthcare she received at birth. They also alleged that their noneconomic damages would greatly exceed 735 ILCS 5/2-1706.5 (2008)'s caps that specifically limited the recovery of such damages in medical malpractice cases. The trial court, ruling on the pleadings, found the statutory caps operated as a "legislative remittitur" that violated the separation-of-powers clause of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. It found the statute unconstitutional facially and as applied, and that its inseverability provision required invalidation of the entire statute. The state supreme court found that since it was facially unconstitutional on separation-of-powers grounds because it was the judiciary's function to reduce verdicts, determining any "as applied" challenge was unnecessary. It thus rejected the healthcare providers' claim that the statute was a valid exercise of the legislature's police powers upon finding the issue was not the wisdom of the law, but whether the law unduly infringed on the judiciary's power.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment finding that the statute limiting awards of noneconomic damages in medical malpractice cases to be unconstitutional "as applied" to the minor and her mother. It affirmed the trial court's finding that the statute was "facially" invalid. It also remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Nelson


Docket No. 105340.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


235 Ill. 2d 386; 922 N.E.2d 1056; 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2308; 337 Ill. Dec. 479



December 17, 2009, Opinion Filed


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Convictions affirmed; sentences affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Will County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of 16 counts of first degree murder in violation of 720 ILCS 5/9-1(a)(1), (a)(2), (a)(3) (2002), four counts of home invasion, and four counts of aggravated arson. The jury then found death to be an appropriate sentence for the murders and the trial court imposed death sentences on those convictions. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of 16 counts of first degree murder, four counts of home invasion in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-11(a)(1) (2002), and four counts of aggravated arson in violation of 720 ILCS 5/20-1.1(a)(1) (2002). Defendant was then sentenced, inter alia, to death for the murders. He raised many issues on appeal, such as the trial court granting the State's motion in limine precluding him from cross-examining two police detectives about an unrelated civil case against them, which the appellate court found not to be error. However, it found the trial court erred in dismissing a juror during sentencing deliberations and in replacing him. It found that the dismissed juror's voir dire answers about the death penalty were inconsistent, not dishonest, and that the dismissed juror engaged in jury deliberations. It further found that since he had appeared ready to sign the non-unanimous jury verdict form, defendant might have received a prison term rather than the death penalty, meaning defendant's Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, due process right to a verdict from the jury chosen was violated and precluded imposition of the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendants convictions, as well as his sentences on the four home invasion and four aggravated arson convictions. It also ordered the case to be remanded to the trial court with directions to vacate defendant's sentence of death and to resentence defendant to a sentence other than death.

People v. K.E.F. (In re K.E.F.)


Docket No. 107402


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


235 Ill. 2d 530; 922 N.E.2d 322; 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2304; 337 Ill. Dec. 199



December 17, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
People v. K.E.F. (In re K.E.F), 231 Ill. 2d 632, 902 N.E.2d 1084, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 113, 327 Ill. Dec. 698 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court affirmed; appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court entered a judgment that granted respondent juvenile's motion to dismiss petitioner State's appeal of the juvenile court's order rendered in a juvenile delinquency proceeding that denied the State's motion to admit certain recorded statements made by the alleged victim. The state supreme court allowed the State's petition for levae to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a delinquency petition in the juvenile court alleging that the juvenile was delinquent because he had committed unlawful restraint and various sexual offenses against his sister. Prior to the adjudicatory hearing, the State sought a ruling on the admissibility of statements the alleged victim had made during an interview with a forensic interviewer. The State presented a DVD of the interview for the juvenile court to consider. At the adjudicatory hearing, the State called the 11-year-old alleged victim as a witness; however, it did not question her about the events and, instead, limited its inquiry to the circumstances surrounding how the videotaped statement was obtained. The trial court then denied the State's motion to admit the recorded statements. The State appealed. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court then found that jurisdiction was lacking under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(1) because the juvenile court's order denying the motion to admit did not suppress evidence given that it merely barred one way in which the factfinder might receive the evidence but still raised the possibility that live testimony could be presented about the statements.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment and dismissed the appeal.

Passalino v. City of Zion


Docket No. 107429


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


237 Ill. 2d 118; 928 N.E.2d 814; 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2307; 340 Ill. Dec. 567



December 17, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing April 22, 2010.
Modified and rehearing denied by Passalino v. City of Zion, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 662 (Ill., Apr. 22, 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois), on plaintiff landowners action to declare invalid defendant city's zoning amendment prohibiting the use of their land to build multifamily buildings, granted their summary judgment motion. In doing so, it found 65 ILCS 5/11-13-2 (1996), about notice of public hearings by newspaper publication, to be unconstitutional as applied to them and that the amendment was void as to their parcel. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: An ordinance allowed the landowners' property allowing to be developed for single-family and multiple use. The landowners built both types of residences on it. The city subsequently decided to adopt a new zoning ordinance. It provided notice in two community newspapers of the desire to adopt the new ordinance, consistent with the notice requirement in 65 ILCS 5/11-13-2 (1996). Multiple parcels of property were affected because parcels were rezoned from multifamily to single-family use. The ordinance passed. About five years later, the landowners discovered they could not develop their remaining property into multifamily units. They sought to have the ordinance amendment declared invalid. The trial court granted their summary judgment motion, found 65 ILCS 5/11-13-2 (1996) was unconstitutional as applied, and declared the ordinance amendment was void as to their parcel. The state supreme court found that the notice given in the two newspapers did not meet Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. XIV, due process standards, as it was not reasonably calculated to give them notice of the public hearing on the proposed ordinance amendment despite that amendment affecting the landowners.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
