People v. Lakisha M. (In re Lakisha M.)


Docket No. 103541.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 259; 882 N.E.2d 570; 2008 Ill. LEXIS 8; 317 Ill. Dec. 690



January 25, 2008, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Lakisha M. (In re Lakisha M.), 222 Ill. 2d 573, 861 N.E.2d 655, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 2071, 308 Ill. Dec. 324 (2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A juvenile court found appellant juvenile guilty of aggravated battery and adjudicated her delinquent. The court ordered the juvenile to submit a saliva sample for deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) analysis and indexing under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3(a)(3.5) (2004) of the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections. The Court of Appeals of Illinois upheld the constitutionality of the DNA indexing statute. The juvenile petitioned for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile contended that the compulsory extraction of her saliva, its analysis for DNA genetic marker groupings, and the perpetual storage and open-ended potential for repeated searches of her genetic profile under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2004) violated her right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amends. IV and XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. She also contended that the statute, when applied to minors adjudicated delinquent, permitted an unreasonable invasion of privacy, in violation of the Privacy Clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. The state supreme court found that the juvenile's right to be free from unreasonable searches under the Fourth Amendment was not violated by the DNA indexing statute. Further, the juvenile was not entitled to greater Fourth Amendment protections by reason of her minority or her status as a nonsexual felony offender. Moreover, there was no basis for interpreting the search and seizure provision of the Illinois Constitution as providing any greater rights to the juvenile than the Fourth Amendment. Finally, the DNA indexing statute did not violate the Privacy Clause of the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

 

157 of 2788 DOCUMENTS



Hudson v. City of Chicago


Docket No. 100466.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


228 Ill. 2d 462; 889 N.E.2d 210; 2008 Ill. LEXIS 12; 321 Ill. Dec. 306



January 25, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hudson v. City of Chi., 2008 Ill. LEXIS 321 (Ill., Apr. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Hudson v. City of Chicago, 216 Ill. 2d 686, 839 N.E.2d 1024, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1226, 298 Ill. Dec. 377 (2005)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the dismissal of a prior suit, plaintiff relatives sued defendants, a city and a fire commissioner, alleging willful and wanton misconduct in providing emergency services to a decedent. The circuit court granted defendants' motion to dismiss pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619 (2006) based on res judicata. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed. The relatives' petition for leave to appeal was allowed.


OVERVIEW: The five-year-old decedent died from acute asthma exacerbation after his mother called 911. In the prior suit, the relatives' negligence count was dismissed and the relatives voluntarily dismissed the remaining willful and wanton misconduct count pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1009 (2000). The relatives refiled their wrongful-death action, setting forth only one count for willful and wanton misconduct. The supreme court determined that res judicata barred the refiled willful and wanton misconduct claim because (1) under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 273, the involuntary dismissal of the negligence claim constituted an adjudication on the merits for res judicata purposes, (2) the willful and wanton count arose out of the same set of operative facts as the negligence count and the relatives could have litigated and resolved the willful and wanton misconduct claim in the prior suit, (3) no exceptions were present, and (4) there was no basis for concluding that the legislature intended in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1009 and 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-217 (1994) to give the relatives an absolute right to split their claims.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.


 

158 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Whitfield


Docket No. 102985.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2007 Ill. LEXIS 1706



December 13, 2007, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Whitfield, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 2047 (Ill., Dec. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Whitfield, 366 Ill. App. 3d 448, 851 N.E.2d 730, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 483, 303 Ill. Dec. 543 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the circuit court to aggravated possession of a stolen motor vehicle. He was sentenced to a term of probation. Defendant's plea was withdrawn, and he was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced to a term of imprisonment. An appellate court (Illinois) ruled that the trial court should have considered granting defendant sentencing credit for his time on probation. The State of Illinois appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the entry of defendant's guilty plea, the State mistakenly advised the trial court that defendant had one prior felony conviction when defendant actually had two prior felony convictions. Defendant was thus ineligible for probation. Subsequently, defendant was convicted and sentenced to a term of prison. He contended that he was entitled to receive credit for the time he had spent on probation. The state supreme court found that the appellate court's order amounted to an unauthorized use of supervisory power under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b) and Ill. Const. art. VI, § 16. Additionally, while 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-7(b) (2004) did confer a mandatory right to sentencing credit, it conferred that right only upon individuals who spent time either in custody, in home detention, in psychiatric confinement, or in substance abuse treatment. Therefore, defendant did not qualify for the mandatory credit. Furthermore, the court could not make laws under Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. Finally, neither defendant's equal protection rights, nor his double jeopardy rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and Ill. Const. art. I, § 10 were violated by defendant not receiving the credit.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's judgment was reversed.

 

159 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Whitfield


Docket No. 102985.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


228 Ill. 2d 502; 888 N.E.2d 1166; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 2047; 321 Ill. Dec. 233



December 13, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing April 23, 2008.
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Whitfield, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 322 (Ill., Apr. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Whitfield, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1706 (Ill., Dec. 13, 2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to probation on his guilty plea to aggravated possession of a stolen motor vehicle. The State learned that defendant was ineligible for probation and the plea was vacated. Defendant was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced to prison. An appellate court (Illinois) concluded that the trial court should have considered granting defendant credit for the time he spent on probation. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer performed a license plate check on a vehicle being driven by defendant, which revealed that the car was stolen. Defendant was arrested. He admitted that he had stollen the victim's car. Relying on criminal history information provided by the State, the trial court sentenced defendant to two years' probation. The State learned that defendant had two prior convictions and moved to vacate defendant's guilty plea, asserting that the sentence was void. Defendant was convicted at trial and was sentenced to eight years' incarceration. On appeal, defendant asserted that the trial court should have considered whether he should receive credit for the time he spent on probation. The appellate court agreed on grounds of fundamental fairness. The supreme court held that neither 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-7(b) (2004) nor 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-6-4(h) (2004) allowed for any discretion to award credit for time spent on probation when defendant was subsequently sentenced to incarceration when the original sentence was illegal. Such resentencing did not violate double jeopardy protections of U.S. Const. amend. V or Ill. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment.

 

160 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Flynn v. Henkel


Docket No. 103946.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 176; 880 N.E.2d 166; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1697; 316 Ill. Dec. 688



November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Flynn v. Henkel, 369 Ill. App. 3d 328, 859 N.E.2d 1063, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1097, 307 Ill. Dec. 386 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee grandmother of a child filed a petition against appellant mother of the child, seeking grandparent visitation of the child pursuant to the grandparents visitation statute, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(a-5) (2006). The trial court allowed the visitation, providing for three hours of unsupervised visitation on the second Saturday of each month. The Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District, affirmed. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not make specific findings as to how the grandmother had overcome the statutory presumption that the mother's decisions regarding grandparent visitation were not harmful to the child's mental, physical, or emotional health. The appellate court found that, although the grandmother testified, inter alia, that the child loved her, she presented no evidence that denial of visitation with her would harm the child's mental, physical, or emotional health. The only evidence relating to such harm came from the mother, who testified that the denial of visitation to the grandmother was not harmful to the child. The trial court found there was no "direct emotional harm" to the child in denying visitation to the grandmother. Neither denial of an opportunity for grandparent visitation, nor a child never knowing a grandparent was "harm" that rebutted the 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(a-5)(3) (2006) presumption that a fit parent's denial of a grandparent's visitation was not harmful to the child's mental, physical, or emotional health. The trial court's ruling that the grandmother had overcome the statutory presumption was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court and the intermediate appellate court were reversed.

 

161 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Sun Life Assur. Co. of Can. v. Manna


Docket No. 103849


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 128; 879 N.E.2d 320; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1699; 316 Ill. Dec. 253



November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Sun Life Assur. Co. of Can. v. Manna, 368 Ill. App. 3d 591, 858 N.E.2d 503, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 996, 306 Ill. Dec. 706 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company (insurer), a Canadian corporation, challenged a judgment of the Illinois Appellate Court, affirming a circuit court judgment finding the Illinois retaliatory tax (215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/444 (2006)) on alien corporations constitutional.


OVERVIEW: This appeal raised three issues: whether the retaliatory tax violated the uniformity clause of the Illinois Constitution (Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970)); whether the U.S. Congress, through the McCarran-Ferguson Act (15 U.S.C.S. § 1012 (2000)), authorized Illinois to impose a retaliatory tax upon the insurer; and, if not, whether the tax violated the so-called Dormant Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution (U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3). The supreme court found the tax was not prohibited by the uniformity clause, as all foreign and alien insurance companies had to pay the tax, regardless of their origin, and its legitimate purpose of equalizing tax burdens between states barred the insurer's challenge. The plain language of the Act imposed no limitation on the imposition of the tax. The Act provided that there would not be any barrier on the regulation of every person involved in the "business of insurance, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 1011, 1012(a) (2000). The supreme court read this to mean that alien insurers were within the ambit of the Act. Congress removed all Commerce Clause limitations on states' authority to regulate and tax the insurance business when it passed the Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

People v. Perkins


Docket No. 103693


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2007 Ill. LEXIS 1703



November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Perkins, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 335 (Ill., May 27, 2008)
Modified by People v. Perkins, 229 Ill. 2d 34, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 2052 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Perkins, 367 Ill. App. 3d 895, 856 N.E.2d 1178, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 919, 306 Ill. Dec. 83 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court vacated the trial court's dismissal of the petition filed by petitioner for postconviction relief and ordered that the case be remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The state supreme court then granted the State's petition for leave to appeal the appellate court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of four crimes and sentenced. On appeal, two convictions were vacated. Only then did he file a postconviction relief petition in the trial court; in it, he alleged a constitutional violation. Counsel was then appointed for him. Petitioner's counsel subsequently filed a certificate in accordance with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) confirming his in-person consultation with petitioner. The State moved to dismiss the petition as untimely. Petitioner's counsel claimed that the time for filing the postconviction petition did not start running until after the appellate court's decision and essentially concluded that petitioner was not culpably negligent for the delay in filing the petition. The trial court, however, dismissed the petition as untimely filed. The appellate court vacated upon finding counsel failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c). On further review, the state supreme court found that petitioner's counsel complied with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) by alleging facts that could establish a lack of culpable negligence regarding the petition's late filing, especially since the record did not show any alternative facts that would excuse the late filing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed and the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Miller


Docket Nos. 104022, 104035 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 185; 879 N.E.2d 292; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1704; 316 Ill. Dec. 225



November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Miller v. Miller, 369 Ill. App. 3d 46, 860 N.E.2d 519, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1140, 307 Ill. Dec. 865 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Attorney General of Illinois and a former wife, challenged a judgment of an appellate court (Illinois), which reversed a trial court judgment imposing statutory penalties under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35 (2004) against appellee, the employer of the wife's former husband, for failure to timely turn over child support payments withheld from the husband's wages.


OVERVIEW: The employer argued that the Withholding Act was unconstitutional as applied to him, depriving him of his due process rights under both U.S. Const., amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970). The trial court applied the statutory $ 100-per-day penalty, resulting in a judgment for $ 1,172,100. The appellate court held that the statutory penalty, as applied in the instant case, was unconstitutionally severe. Reversing the appellate court's judgment, the court held that the statute did not violate the employer's substantive due process rights. A state's interest in the support of children was compelling. Further, as applied to the employer, the statute was not unconstitutional. During the two and a half year period relevant to the litigation, the employer violated the Withholding Act on 11,721 separate occasions. The employer was aware of his statutory obligations and of the penalty. Nonetheless, he repeatedly and knowingly violated the statute. Because the employer controlled the extent of the penalty, he could not complain that the penalty was harsh when compared to the amount of child support at issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed that of the trial court.

People v. Rivera


Docket No. 98609


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 1; 879 N.E.2d 876; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1705; 316 Ill. Dec. 488



November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Rivera v. Illinois, 129 S. Ct. 29, 171 L. Ed. 2d 932, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5445 (U.S., 2008)
Motion granted by People v. Rivera, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1255, 327 Ill. Dec. 361 (Ill., 2009)
Affirmed by Rivera v. Illinois, 129 S. Ct. 1446, 173 L. Ed. 2d 320, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 2495 (U.S., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Rivera, 221 Ill. 2d 481, 852 N.E.2d 771, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1094, 304 Ill. Dec. 315 (2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of two counts of first degree murder by the trial court. His conviction was affirmed by the Appellate Court (Illinois). He had argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred when it sua sponte raised a reverse-Batson challenge to his use of a peremptory challenge during jury selection and that the imposition of his extended-term sentence violated the rule announced in Apprendi. He again appealed.


OVERVIEW: During jury selection, defense counsel questioned a juror who worked at a hospital which was known for treating gunshot victims. The judge prohibited defendant from using a peremptory challenge to reject the juror. The Illinois Supreme Court held the judge improperly used counsel's response to his command as a basis for finding a prima facie case of discrimination. The record did not support the action taken by the trial court. Since women outnumbered men on the venire two to one, it would not be unusual, from a statistical standpoint, that defendant had used peremptory challenges against two women and one man prior to consideration of the juror at issue. The fact that she had frequent contact with gunshot victims seemed to a valid reason why defense counsel might want to excuse her, and defense counsel's questioning revealed nothing of a discriminatory nature. However, the evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming, and the error in denying defendant's peremptory challenge was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The Apprendi violation was also harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was affirmed, though not the entirety of its analysis, insofar as that judgment affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Townsend v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


Docket No. 103858.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 147; 879 N.E.2d 893; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1701; 316 Ill. Dec. 505; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,880



November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Townsend v. Sears, Roebuck & Co., 368 Ill. App. 3d 902, 858 N.E.2d 552, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1005, 306 Ill. Dec. 755 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment vacated; circuit court order vacated; cause remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court entered a judgment that found the trial court correctly ruled when the trial court determined that Illinois law governed the substantive issues of liability and damages in plaintiff family's personal injury action filed on behalf of the minor son. The case involved contacts with Michigan and Illinois. Defendant retailer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The family resided in Michigan. The father obtained a riding lawn tractor from the retailer in Michigan. The retailer was a New York corporation domiciled in Illinois and made certain decisions regarding the design of the riding lawn tractor, product testing, distribution of that product, and investigations involving injuries caused by the product in Illinois. The father was mowing his lawn in Michigan using the riding lawn tractor. He did not see his minor son, who was less than four-years-old, walk up behind the riding lawn tractor. The father then backed up and ran over the minor son with the riding lawn tractor. The family sued the retailer in Illinois, alleged strict products liability and negligence claims, and moved to apply Illinois law to the liability and damages issues. The trial court ruled that Illinois law applied to those substantive issues and the appellate court agreed. On further review, the state supreme court found that Illinois' relationship to the case was not so pivotal as to overcome the presumption that Michigan, as the state where the injury occurred and the family resided, was the state with the most significant relationship to the case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment and the trial court's order were vacated and case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Wade v. City of N. Chicago Police Pension Bd.


Docket No. 101265.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


226 Ill. 2d 485; 877 N.E.2d 1101; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1694; 315 Ill. Dec. 772



November 1, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Wade v. City of N. Chi. Police Pension Bd., 359 Ill. App. 3d 224, 833 N.E.2d 427, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 793, 295 Ill. Dec. 594 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer applied for a disability pension with defendant City of North Chicago Police Pension Board. The officer's counsel requested limited consideration for a duty-related disability pension only under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1 (2002). The Board denied the officer a line-of-duty pension. The circuit court confirmed the Board's decision. The appellate court (Illinois) upheld the Board's decision. The officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The officer, who had prior knee problems, suffered a new injury to his knee while transporting a prisoner. The evidence adduced in the instant case included testimony from five doctors, four of whom found the officer to be disabled such that the officer was unable to perform in a full-duty capacity as a police officer. Two of those doctors specifically found that the subject injury aggravated the officer's preexisting condition, rendering him disabled. The sole doctor who opined that the officer was not disabled for full duty as a police officer provided no factual basis for his conclusion that the tears to the officer's knee that were treated by another doctor were a preexisting disease and not traumatic tears caused by a new injury. Other than his opinion, there was no medical evidence whatsoever to support a finding that the officer was not disabled for full duty as a police officer, and there was abundant medical evidence that the officer was disabled. The supreme court further concluded that it was not necessary for all three of the Board-selected physicians to concur and that the credible assessments of two of three Board-appointed physicians supported a pension award.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the circuit and appellate courts were reversed, the decision of the Board was set aside, and the cause was remanded to the Board with directions that it grant the employee a line-of-duty pension in accordance with 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1 (2002).

 

167 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Devine v. Stralka


Docket No. 102962.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


226 Ill. 2d 445; 877 N.E.2d 416; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1693; 315 Ill. Dec. 664



October 18, 2007, Opinion Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A juvenile was adjudicated delinquent for the unauthorized possession or storage of a weapon under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/21-6 (2004). The trial court accepted the juvenile's guilty plea and sentenced him to 12 months of probation and other conditions. Nearly one year later, the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted the juvenile's motion to vacate the delinquency finding. Petitioner State sought a writ of mandamus or prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court exceeded its authority when it vacated the delinquency finding over 11 months after the juvenile pled guilty and was sentenced for the offense. The supreme court held that the delinquency finding was not subject to modification 11 months after the juvenile was sentenced to probation. While the juvenile sentencing disposition was a final and appealable order and the trial court retained jurisdiction to modify the sentencing disposition and wardship, nothing in the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987 gave the trial court the authority to modify the finding of delinquency once the disposition became final and appealable. The supreme court further noted that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2004) petitions were applicable to juvenile cases and that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) strictly applied to juvenile cases. The juvenile did not file a petition under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2004), nor did he file a motion to vacate his guilty plea under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d). In addition, the order vacating the delinquency finding interfered with the statutory scheme for expungement of juvenile law enforcement and court records.


OUTCOME: The writ of prohibition was allowed and the trial court was directed to reinstate the finding of delinquency against the juvenile and to vacate the portion of its order that vacated the juvenile's delinquency finding.

Felzak v. Hruby


Docket No. 103755.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


226 Ill. 2d 382; 876 N.E.2d 650; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1158; 315 Ill. Dec. 338



September 20, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Felzak v. Hruby, 367 Ill. App. 3d 695, 855 N.E.2d 202, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 812, 305 Ill. Dec. 311 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment vacated; circuit court judgment vacated; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee grandmother sued appellant parents, pursuant 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607.1 (2004) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, to enforce an agreed visitation order. The circuit court denied the parents' motion to dismiss and held the parents in indirect civil contempt for failing to follow the order. The Court of Appeals of Illinois affirmed the judgment of the circuit court. The parents petitioned for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother sought to enforce an order agreed to between the grandmother and the parents which allowed her to visit her granddaughter. By the time the case reached the state supreme court, the granddaughter had reached the age of majority. The state supreme court found that because the parents could no longer compel the daughter to visit the grandmother, the rationale for the civil contempt order in the case was lost. When such a situation occurred, the appropriate disposition of the case was to vacate the judgments of the lower courts and remand the cause with instructions to dismiss because the issues raised in the contempt proceedings were necessarily moot. Similarly, the issues presented by the circuit court's ruling on the grandmother's petition to enforce the agreed visitation order were also moot because the courts could not force the granddaughter, who was then an adult, to visit the grandmother. As with the contempt proceedings, the cause was to be remanded to the circuit court with instructions to dismiss the petition to enforce.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the appellate and circuit courts were vacated. The cause was remanded to the circuit court with instructions to dismiss the grandmother's petition for rule to show cause and her petition to enforce the agreed order.

People v. LaPointe

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


227 Ill. 2d 39; 879 N.E.2d 275; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1161; 316 Ill. Dec. 208



September 20, 2007, Opinion Filed

People v. LaPointe, 365 Ill. App. 3d 914, 850 N.E.2d 893, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 532, 303 Ill. Dec. 88 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court entered a judgment that affirmed the trial court's ruling that denied petitioner's leave to file a second postconviction petition in a case where petitioner had pled guilty to the murder of a taxi driver and was eventually sentenced to natural life in prison. The state supreme court granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty to the murder of a taxi driver and eventually received a natural life sentence. He later began filing a series of collateral challenges. Among other filings, he submitted a first postconviction petition. The trial court dismissed that petition and the appellate court affirmed. Thereafter, a county clerk file stamped his second petition for postconviction relief, which had been received by the clerk's office in the mail. Ann. 5/122-1(f) (2004), the second petition could not be considered to be filed because the required leave of court had not been obtained.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

Ultsch v. Ill. Mun. Ret. Fund


Docket No. 102232.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


226 Ill. 2d 169; 874 N.E.2d 1; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1148; 314 Ill. Dec. 91



August 2, 2007, Opinion Filed


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff claimant's complaint for administrative review of defendant retirement fund's denial of the claimant's application for temporary disability benefits based on the trial court's ruling that Ill. Pub. Act 89-685 (1997), amending the state's administrative review law, was unconstitutional. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant applied to the retirement fund for temporary disability benefits; the retirement fund denied the application. The claimant appealed to the retirement fund's board of trustees, which adopted as its final decision its committee's recommendation that the application be denied. The claimant then filed a complaint for administrative review of the denial of her claim. The complaint named the retirement fund as the sole defendant. The retirement fund moved to dismiss because the claimant did not name the board of trustees as a defendant. The trial court dismissed the complaint based on its ruling that Ill. Pub. Act 89-685 (1997), amending the state's administrative review law, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the state supreme court found that it did not need to address the constitutional issue because dismissal was required pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-103(2) (2004) and 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-107(a) (2004), read together, once the claimant failed to include the retirement fund's board of trustees as a necessary party given that it had issued the final decision in the case.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's decision that granted the retirement fund's motion to dismiss the claimant's complaint for administrative review. As a result, the state supreme court vacated the trial court's judgment declaring Ill. Pub. Act 89-685 unconstitutional.

 

171 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Melchor


Docket No. 101772.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


226 Ill. 2d 24; 871 N.E.2d 32; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 861; 312 Ill. Dec. 632



June 7, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended August 1, 2007.
On remand at, Remanded by People v. Melchor, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1051 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Melchor, 362 Ill. App. 3d 335, 841 N.E.2d 420, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1123, 299 Ill. Dec. 8 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Vacated and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of first degree murder. Finding that the admission of certain evidence violated defendant's constitutional rights, an appellate court (Illinois) reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. The State's petition for leave to appeal was allowed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to appear after positing bond on the 1990 murder charge. He was arrested in 2000 on an outstanding warrant. On appeal, defendant argued that the admission of the 1991 testimony of a deceased eyewitness, given in a codefendant's trial, violated defendant's Confrontation Clause rights. The trial court found the testimony admissible under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10.4 (2004). The appellate court reversed on the constitutional issue, holding that its decision rendered the issue of the admissibility under § 115-10.4 moot. The supreme court vacated that judgment. Courts were to avoid reaching constitutional issues if rulings could be made on another basis. In the instant case, the appellate court should have first determined if the trial court's evidentiary ruling was erroneous. If so, the next question was whether the error was harmless. If the ruling was erroneous and was not harmless, the case would end and defendant would be entitled to a new trial. Only if the trial court's § 115-10.4 ruling was not erroneous, or was erroneous but harmless as an evidentiary matter, should the appellate court have turned to the constitutional challenge to the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was vacated and the cause was remanded to the appellate court with directions that the court first consider the nonconstitutional issues raised, reaching the constitutional issues only if necessary.

People v. Hauschild


Docket No. 102468


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


226 Ill. 2d 63; 871 N.E.2d 1; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 862; 312 Ill. Dec. 601



June 7, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended August 1, 2007.
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Hauschild, 2015 IL App (2d) 131040-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2705 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Hauschild, 364 Ill. App. 3d 202, 845 N.E.2d 74, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 176, 300 Ill. Dec. 653 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) entered a judgment that affirmed defendant's convictions for attempted murder, armed robbery, home invasion, and criminal damage to property, and the related sentences for home invasion and criminal damage to property, but vacated defendant's sentences for attempted murder and armed robbery. The state supreme court granted defendant's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a codefendant broke into a residence, confronted a man and his wife, demanded a safe, and fired their weapons. Two shots hit the man. Defendant and the codefendant fled, and took a lockbox with them. The codefendant later pled guilty to charges against him and testified against defendant. Defendant was tried before a jury. He was convicted of attempted murder, armed robbery, home invasion, and criminal damage to property. On appeal, the appellate court vacated his nonenhanced sentenced for attempted murder and directed the trial court to add a mandatory 15-year enhancement for weapon possession. It also vacated his armed robbery sentence. On further review, the state supreme court found that in light of its recent Sharpe decision, which was decided while defendant's case was pending on review, the 15-year enhancement could be added to the attempted murder sentence, that such an enhancement to the armed robbery sentence would make that sentence disproportionate to the offense of armed violence predicated on robbery with a certain type of weapon, and that defendant's heavier sentence when compared with that of his codefendant was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment vacating defendant's nonenhanced sentence for attempted murder and directing the trial court to add the mandated 15-year sentence to the new base sentence was affirmed. Its judgment vacating defendant's sentence for armed robbery was affirmed, but its resentencing directive on remand was reversed with directions. Otherwise, the appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

 

173 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


Docket No. 102096.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


225 Ill. 2d 573; 870 N.E.2d 415; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 858; 312 Ill. Dec. 350



May 24, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended July 31, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Johnson, 363 Ill. App. 3d 356, 843 N.E.2d 434, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 40, 300 Ill. Dec. 176 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which ruled that the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq. (2000) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. Defendant had been convicted of aggravated kidnapping of a grandmother and granddaughter and had been required to register as a sex offender under the Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the definition of a sex offense in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/2(B)(1.5) (2000) was unconstitutional as applied to him because the aggravated kidnapping of the granddaughter was not sexually motivated. The supreme court reversed, finding first that amendments to the Act while the State's appeal was pending that, inter alia, changed the definition of "sex offense" to include only sexually motivated aggravated kidnappings of a minor by a non-parent, did not preclude review of the constitutional issue presented. The pre-amendment version of § 2(B)(1.5) satisfied the rational basis test. The Act's purpose of assisting law enforcement and protecting the public was a legitimate state interest. The state legislature chose to include aggravated kidnapping of a minor by a non-parent in the definition of a sex offense, and, consequently, to impose a registration requirement under the Act on persons convicted of such an offense, regardless of whether their conduct was sexually motivated. The decision was a reasonable one that satisfied the second prong of the rational basis test. Thus, the Act was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated a finding by the appellate court that the aggravated kidnapping was not sexually motivated. The supreme court then reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for issuance of an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) certificate.

People v. Hampton


Docket No. 102413


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


225 Ill. 2d 238; 867 N.E.2d 957; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 451; 310 Ill. Dec. 906



April 19, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended June 14, 2007.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by People v. Hampton, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1349 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
People v. Hampton, 363 Ill. App. 3d 293, 842 N.E.2d 1124, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 131, 299 Ill. Dec. 772 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed as of right after an appellate court (Illinois) ruled that the 15-year mandatory sentencing enhancement for aggravated criminal sexual assault while armed with a firearm found in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14(d)(1) (2002) violated the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of eight counts of criminal sexual assault and two counts of home invasion. He was sentenced to consecutive terms of 21 years' imprisonment on four of the sexual assault convictions. Before reaching the proportionate penalties clause argument, the appellate court vacated defendant's convictions and remanded for determination of whether a Crawford violation occurred and whether defendant forfeited his right to confrontation by wrongdoing. The State's sole contention was that the appellate court erred in finding the sentencing provision unconstitutional. The supreme court agreed. Ruling on the sentencing provision's constitutionality was unnecessary as it could not be assumed that defendant would be convicted again on remand. If defendant was not convicted of the offenses, he would never be subject to sentencing under the 15-year firearm penalty enhancement. Thus, it was unnecessary for the appellate court to address the constitutional issue and declare § 12-14(d)(1) unconstitutional. The appellate court should have declined to address the constitutional issue after vacating defendant's convictions and remanding for a hearing on forfeiture by wrongdoing.


OUTCOME: The State's appeal was dismissed and that portion of the appellate court's judgment addressing issues other than the confrontation clause claim and the possible forfeiture of that claim by wrongdoing, was vacated.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by, Motion denied by Estate of Lowe v. Apex Tax Invs., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10849 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Apex Tax Invs., Inc. v. Lowe (In re County Collector), 217 Ill. 2d 1, 838 N.E.2d 907, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1605, 298 Ill. Dec. 14 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling that denied appellant public guardian's amended petition to set aside a tax deed. People v. Brown


Docket No. 100956.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


225 Ill. 2d 188; 866 N.E.2d 1163; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 449; 310 Ill. Dec. 561



April 5, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended May 31, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Brown, 358 Ill. App. 3d 56, 831 N.E.2d 24, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 568, 294 Ill. Dec. 501 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court reversed the trial court's summary dismissal of defendant's successive petition for post-conviction relief where defendant was convicted of committing attempted murder of a police officer at a time when he was 16-years-old and the statute under which his case was transferred from juvenile court to criminal court was later declared invalid. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in prison serving a 28-year sentence for attempted murder of a police officer, a crime he committed in 1997 at the age of 16. He was convicted after his case was transferred from the juvenile court to the criminal court. Years later, he filed a successive petition for post-conviction relief, which the trial court summarily denied. The appellate court reversed and remanded for a new transfer hearing in accordance with the law currently in effect. On further, the state supreme court found that the issue presented by his case was whether he should be granted postconviction relief on the grounds that the statute under which he was transferred from juvenile custody to criminal court, and subsequently sentenced, was declared invalid in Cervantes. The state supreme court found that he was entitled to relief because the invalidity of the statute meant that it was though the statute had never been enacted. The state supreme court then found that the law in effect at the time of the transfer decision, absent that statute because it was invalid, had to be applied and that defendant might be entitled to relief as a result.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment that reversed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's successive petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed; however, the appellate court's reliance on an ex post facto rationale and vacation of defendant's judgment of conviction for attempted murder of a police officer outright were reversed. Too, the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Mulay v. Mulay


Docket No. 102619


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


225 Ill. 2d 601; 870 N.E.2d 328; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 442; 312 Ill. Dec. 263



March 22, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Mulay v. Mulay, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 2066 (Ill., May 29, 2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Mulay v. Stessman, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2526, 2011 IL App (3d) 100571-U (2011)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandparents appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which found that the statute governing grandparent visitation, § 607(a-5) of the Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(a-5) (Supp. 2005), was facially unconstitutional and dismissed a visitation petition. Appellee mother had sought dismissal of the petition under both 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-615 and 2-619 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court allowed the Illinois Attorney General to intervene. The Attorney General argued that the trial court improperly ruled on the constitutionality of the statute when nonconstitutional grounds were available. The supreme court agreed. Illinois courts were to address constitutional issues only as a last resort. The trial court ruled on the 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619 (2004) motion without first addressing the facial sufficiency of the grandparents' petition under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-615 (2004). The supreme court rejected the mother's argument that there was a tacit denial of the § 2-615 motion. There was no support in the record for that argument, and the supreme court would not presume an implicit denial of the § 2-615 motion. The supreme court also rejected the notion that the mother's fundamental parental rights were infringed upon by the filing of the visitation petition by the grandparents. Nothing in the Lulay decision categorically forbid litigation requiring a parental response because it constituted a significant interference with the fundamental rights of parents.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

179 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Delgado v. Bd. of Election Comm'rs


No. 104112


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


224 Ill. 2d 481; 865 N.E.2d 183; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 439; 309 Ill. Dec. 820



February 23, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 07 COEL 02. Hon. Nathaniel R. Howse, Jr., Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens challenged appellee candidate's nomination papers with appellee election board. The board overruled the objection, found that the papers were valid, and ordered that the candidate's name be printed on a ballot. The citizens filed a complaint in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for judicial review. The circuit court affirmed the order of the election board. The citizens appealed under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Because the candidate was a convicted felon, whose right to hold municipal office had not been restored under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/29-15 (2004), he was ineligible to hold elective municipal office under 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3.1-10-5 (2004) of the Illinois Municipal Code. The election board however concluded that 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3.1-10-5(b) was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection. The state supreme court found that the board's decision was void and a nullity because, in ruling as it did, the board exceeded its authority under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-10 (2004) of the Illinois Election Code, 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-1 et seq. (2004). Further, in affirming the board's decision, the circuit court failed to comply with the formalities of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 18. Furthermore, even if the circuit court had some justification for reaching the constitutionality of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3.1-10-5(b), it had no proper basis for holding that the statute violated equal protection guarantees. Finally, the court found that the litigation was properly disposed of through a supervisory order rather than a direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed, the judgment of the circuit court was to be vacated, and the case was to be remanded to the circuit court with instructions to vacate the election board's decision and direct the board to declare that the candidate was ineligible to run, reject his nomination papers, and remove his name from the ballot. If removal of the name could not be accomplished prior to election, the board was to disregard any votes cast for him.

People v. Suarez


Docket No. 100499.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


224 Ill. 2d 37; 862 N.E.2d 977; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 5; 308 Ill. Dec. 774



January 19, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Suarez, 238 Ill. App. 3d 110, 606 N.E.2d 1237, 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1592, 180 Ill. Dec. 160 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate's first postconviction petition, alleging ineffective assistance of trial counsel, was dismissed as untimely. The appellate court affirmed. The inmate filed a pro se petition, alleging that the statute under which he was sentenced violated Apprendi. The circuit court appointed counsel, who filed a supplemental petition. That petition was dismissed. The appellate court (Illinois) affirmed. The inmate was granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the appellate court erred in finding that postconviction counsel's failure to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) constituted harmless error. The State argued that application of harmless error review was appropriate because counsel could do nothing to shape defendant's noncognizable Apprendi claim into a meritorious issue. The supreme court held that the appellate court erred in applying a harmless error analysis where no compliance with Rule 651(c) was shown. The supreme court noted that compliance had to be shown regardless of whether the claims made in the pro se or amended petition were viable. The supreme court's analysis was driven by the conviction that where postconviction counsel does not adequately complete the duties mandated by the rule, the limited right to counsel conferred by the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (2000), could not be fully realized.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court court was reversed and the case was remanded to the circuit court for the purpose of demonstrating compliance with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c). The appellate court decisions in People v. Sargent, 357 Ill. App. 3d 946, 294 Ill. Dec. 272 (2005) and People v. Oakes, 355 Il.. App. 3d 748, 291 Ill. Dec. 784 (2005) were overruled to the extent those cases were in conflict.

GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd.


Docket Nos. 101585, 101601 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


224 Ill. 2d 1; 862 N.E.2d 209; 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1; 308 Ill. Dec. 611



January 8, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended March 12, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd., 361 Ill. App. 3d 271, 836 N.E.2d 903, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1028, 297 Ill. Dec. 172 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Existing car dealerships filed a protest against proposed dealerships with appellee State of Illinois Motor Vehicle Review Board, pursuant to the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 710/1 et seq. (2004). Appellants, a manufacturer and a new dealership, appealed. The appellate court (Illinois) affirmed. The manufacturer and the new dealership appealed.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer sought to add two dealerships within the existing dealerships' relevant market area. On appeal, the manufacturer argued that the Board did not apply the "good cause" standard correctly. The supreme court disagreed, noting that the legislature intended that the Board balance the dealer's interest in maintaining viable businesses, the manufacturer's interest in promoting sales, and the public's interest in adequate competition and convenient sales. The supreme court further concluded that the Board's decision was not clearly erroneous, noting that there was unrebutted testimony establishing that the existing dealerships had made substantial investments in the dealerships, the existing dealerships had adequate sales and service facilities, and there was no evidence that the existing dealerships had materially breached their franchise agreements. The manufacturer also argued, inter alia, that the Act violated the Commerce Clause by improperly favoring purely local interests. The supreme court found that the Act passed muster under the Pike test because any burden the Act placed on interstate commerce was not clearly excessive in relation to the local benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

People v. E.H. (In re E.H.)

224 Ill. 2d 172; 863 N.E.2d 231; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1666; 309 Ill. Dec. 1



December 21, 2006, Opinion Filed

On remand at, Remanded by People v. E.H. (In re E.H.), 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 724 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.

OVERVIEW: During defendant juvenile's trial for engaging in numerous instances of improper sexual conduct with the minor victims while she was their baby-sitter, the trial court determined that the victims' out-of-court statements to their grandmother were admissible under § 115-10. 184 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rodney H. (In re Rodney H.)


Docket No. 101385.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 510; 861 N.E.2d 623; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1667; 308 Ill. Dec. 292



December 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended February 27, 2007.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellee juvenile admitted guilt to a probation violation, the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) sua sponte declared 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-710(1)(a)(iv) (2004) of the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987 and 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/5(l) (2004) of the Illinois Children and Family Services Act unconstitutional under the Proportionate Penalties Clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The State appealed; appellee cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: At appellee's dispositional hearing after his admission of guilt, the trial court determined that it could not place him with the county because, due a lack of funds, the county had ordered a freeze ordered on all further juvenile placements. Further, it could not order residential placement through the Illinois Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS) because 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-710(1)(a)(iv) and 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/5(l) did not allow DCFS to accept guardianship of delinquent minors over age 13. The trial court held that those provisions violated the Proportionate Penalties Clause due to their disparate treatment of delinquent minors under and over age 13. The high court disagreed. Because a petition for adjudication of wardship was not a direct action by the State to inflict punishment, neither the Proportionate Penalties Clause nor the Cruel and Unusual Punishment Clause applied. The county's failure to appropriate reasonable funds to care for delinquent minors might violate 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/6-7(1) (2004), but that did not mean that § 6-7(1), 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 6-8(2) (2004), or 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-710(1)(a)(iv) were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court, which was free to fashion any disposition consistent with statutory directives. Appellee's request to terminate his wardship was denied, but the trial court was free to grant that relief since appellee was no longer a minor.

 

185 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


Docket No. 101996.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 569; 861 N.E.2d 967; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1671; 308 Ill. Dec. 402



December 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended February 27, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Jones, 218 Ill. 2d 550, 850 N.E.2d 811, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 522, 303 Ill. Dec. 6 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State was granted an appeal as of right to challenge the judgment of the appellate court (Illinois), which held that the monetary charge assessed against defendant, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1(c) (2004), was unconstitutional and that several other charges were satisfied by credit from presentencing incarceration. Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance and cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not challenge his conviction of his sentence of two years' imprisonment on appeal. As such, the court noted that the appeal only involved the issues arising from the monetary charges imposed by the trial court. The trial court relied directly on two case law precedents in holding that the Trauma Fund Spinal Cord charge under § 5/5-9-1.1(c) was unconstitutional and that the drug assessment under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/411.2(a)(4) (2004), was subject to offset by the presentencing incarceration credit. The trial court also held that defendant was entitled to credit against the $ 4 Criminal/Traffic Conviction Surcharge under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1(c-9) (2004), and the $ 100 Trauma Fund charge under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1(b) (2004), which the appellate court also found were fines. The court agreed that the various charges against defendant were fines subject to offset. The court disagreed that the $ 5 charge under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1(c) (2004) violated defendant's substantive due process since the fine was not grossly disproportionate and was rationally related to the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the judgment of the appellate court as to its determination that the Traffic and Criminal Conviction Surcharge, the drug assessment, and the Trauma Fund charge were subject to offset for presentencing incarceration credit. Accordingly, defendant was entitled to a credit of $ 604. The court reversed the appellate court's determination that the Trauma Fund Spinal Cord statute was unconstitutional.

Krautsack v. Anderson


Docket No. 101718.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 541; 861 N.E.2d 633; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1676; 308 Ill. Dec. 302



December 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended March 15, 2007. Counsel Amended February 27, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Krautsack v. Anderson, 218 Ill. 2d 541, 850 N.E.2d 808, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 412, 303 Ill. Dec. 3 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a travel agency and its owner, were granted leave to appeal the judgment of the appellate court (Illinois), which affirmed a trial court judgment in their favor but also affirmed an order striking their fee petition. Plaintiff traveler cross-appealed. Plaintiff's suit alleged breach of contract and violations of the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/1 et seq. (2004).


OVERVIEW: The suit arose from plaintiff's dissatisfaction with a safari trip to East Africa, which was arranged by defendants. The trip was befallen by heavy rains and, upon return, plaintiff demanded a refund from defendants, which defendants refused to do. After a bench trial, the judgment was entered in favor of defendants, but defendants' fee petition, seeking fees and costs over $ 30,000 was stricken upon the trial court determining that defendants failed to satisfy the requirements of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 137 in that defendant failed to allege any false statements by plaintiff and no bad faith was shown entitling them to an award of attorneys fees to the prevailing party under 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/10a(c) (2004). The court held that where a prevailing defendant petitions the trial court for a reasonable attorney fee under § 10a(c), only if the trial court makes a threshold finding that the plaintiff acted in bad faith should the trial court consider other circumstances relevant to its exercise of discretion. Further, defendants failed to demonstrate any bad faith under the requirements of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 137 to entitle them to an award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

187 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Int'l Union of Operating Eng'rs, Local 150 v. Lowe Excavating Co.


Docket Nos. 101231, 101347 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


225 Ill. 2d 456; 870 N.E.2d 303; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1657; 312 Ill. Dec. 238; 181 L.R.R.M. 2015; 153 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P10,768



November 30, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Counsel Amended July 31, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Int'l Union of Operating Eng'rs, Local 150 v. Lowe Excavating Co., 2007 Ill. LEXIS 2069 (Ill., May 29, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lowe Excavating Co. v. Int'l Union of Operating Eng'rs, Local 150, 552 U.S. 1099, 128 S. Ct. 908, 169 L. Ed. 2d 730, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 187 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Lowe Excavating Co. v. Int'l Union of Operating Eng'rs Local No. 150, 358 Ill. App. 3d 1034, 832 N.E.2d 495, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 722, 295 Ill. Dec. 344 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company filed suit against defendant union alleging that the union picketed a company's work site with placards containing false information. The trial court ruled in favor of the union and the appellate court, Illinois, reversed. On remand, the trial court awarded the company compensatory and punitive damages. The appellate court reduced the punitive damages award. The instant court granted the parties' petitions for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The union argued that the appellate court erred in affirming the trial court's punitive damages award, as the damages imposed were unconstitutionally excessive in violation of due process. The company countered that the appellate court erred in reducing the punitive damages award and asserted that it was entitled to a greater amount of punitive damages. The instant court first found that the appellate court erred in finding that the company was financially vulnerable. The instant court reasoned that the record contained no evidence that the company lost other contracts or was unable to perform excavating work at other locations as a result of the union's conduct. The instant court also found that it agreed with the appellate court's conclusion that the union acted with intentional malice. The facts of this case demonstrated that a business agent for the union either knew that the statements contained on his picket signs were false or, at the very least, seriously doubted their veracity. Finally, the instant court found that a punitive damages award of $ 325,000, at a ratio of approximately 75 to 1, was unconstitutionally excessive in light of the union's conduct in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed. The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed as modified by a reduction in the award of punitive damages from $ 325,000 to $ 50,000.

 

188 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Marconi v. Chicago Heights Police Pension Bd.


Docket No. 101418.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2006 Ill. LEXIS 1648



October 19, 2006, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by Marconi v. Chi. Heights Police Pension Bd., 2006 Ill. LEXIS 2098 (Ill., Oct. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Marconi v. Chi. Heights Police Pension Bd., 361 Ill. App. 3d 1, 836 N.E.2d 705, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 925, 296 Ill. Dec. 954 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed in part and vacated in part; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Chicago Heights Police Pension Board sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court of Illinois that, in part, reversed the decision affirming the Board's denial of a disability pension and that declared 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (2002) unconstitutional as applied to the applicant.


OVERVIEW: The applicant made threats of bodily harm against the police chief while in therapy, and the applicant was placed on disability leave. The applicant then sought duty-related disability pension benefits. Three medical experts found that the applicant was disabled due to psychological disorders. The fourth doctor, to whom the applicant was referred by the Board, found that the applicant was not disabled and that the applicant was exaggerating his symptoms. The factual determination of the Board, that the applicant failed to satisfy his burden of proof in establishing his eligibility for a disability pension under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1, 3-114.2 (2002), was not against the manifest weight of the evidence under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-110 (2002). The expert opinions conflicted as to whether the applicant was disabled, creating an issue of fact for the Board to resolve. The Board's resolution was supported by evidence in the record. The fourth doctor's report was replete with expressions of doubt as to whether the applicant suffered from a psychological disturbance and whether he was disabled, and these expressions were supported by specific references to the record.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed with regard to the applicant's administrative review action and was vacated with regard to the determination that 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (2002) was unconstitutional as applied to the applicant. The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

189 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. McCarty


Docket Nos. 100469, 100813 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 109; 858 N.E.2d 15; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1649; 306 Ill. Dec. 570



October 19, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at McCarty v. Buscher, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 124147 (S.D. Ill., Dec. 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
People v. McCarty, 356 Ill. App. 3d 552, 826 N.E.2d 957, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 255, 292 Ill. Dec. 521 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2005)
People v. Reynolds, 358 Ill. App. 3d 286, 831 N.E.2d 1103, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 511, 294 Ill. Dec. 778 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After separate bench trials, defendants were convicted of knowingly manufacturing more than 900 grams of a substance containing methamphetamine under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401(a)(6.5)(D) (2000). Each received the mandatory minimum sentence of 15 years' imprisonment under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401(a)(6.5)(D) (2000). In separate decisions, the Appellate Court (Illinois) affirmed. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to defendants' contention, the supreme court concluded that, for purposes of § 401(a)(6.5)(D) of the Controlled Substances Act, codified at 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401(a)(6.5)(D) (2000), "substance containing methamphetamine" included the byproduct produced during the manufacture of methamphetamine. Accordingly, any byproduct containing traces of methamphetamine qualified as a "substance containing methamphetamine." The supreme court further held that § 401(a)(6.5)(D) did not violate the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, or the due process clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. Among other things, the supreme court noted that methamphetamine manufacturing was a dangerous process and thus, the sentencing category established by § 401(a)(6.5)(D) was not cruel or degrading or a shock to the moral sense of the community. In addition, that section was reasonably designed to remedy to particular evils the legislature was targeting. Finally, the supreme court hold that the search warrant at issue did not violate the warrant clause of the Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 or the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the appellate court were affirmed.

Marconi v. Chicago Heights Police Pension Bd.


Docket No. 101418.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


225 Ill. 2d 497; 870 N.E.2d 273; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 2098; 312 Ill. Dec. 208



October 19, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Modified on Denial of Rehearing May 29, 2007. As Corrected June 6, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Marconi v. Chicago Heights Police Pension Bd., 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1648 (Ill., Oct. 19, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed in part and vacated in part; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court entered a judgment that reversed appellant police pension board's (Board) denial of plaintiff former police officer's disability pension claim after the trial court had confirmed the Board's decision on administrative review. The appellate court also declared 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (2002) unconstitutional as to him. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former police officer, who had problems with the police chief and who had been involved in a troubled relationship with a girlfriend, filed an application for a disability pension with the police pension board (Board). Following a hearing, the Board denied his application. The former police officer thereafter filed an action for administrative review in the trial court. The trial court ultimately confirmed the Board's decision. As a result, it found that it was unnecessary to determine whether the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment that reversed the Board's denial of the former police officer's disability pension claim was reversed. Also, the portion of the appellate court's judgment holding a section of the Pension Code unconstitutional as applied to the former police officer was vacated. Too, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

City of Chicago v. Pooh Bah Enters.


Docket No. 99804.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


224 Ill. 2d 390; 865 N.E.2d 133; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1632; 309 Ill. Dec. 770



October 5, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 14, 2007.
Rehearing denied by City of Chicago v. Pooh Bah Enters., 224 Ill. 2d 390, 865 N.E.2d 133, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 441, 309 Ill. Dec. 770 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Pooh Bah Enters. v. City of Chicago, 552 U.S. 941, 128 S. Ct. 127, 169 L. Ed. 2d 244, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11103 (2007)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by City of Chi. v. Pooh Bah Enters., 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2850 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: City of Chi. v. Pooh Bah Enters., 352 Ill. App. 3d 1217, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 5000 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court of Illinois held that Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 4-60-140(d) did not violate either the federal or the Illinois Constitution. The Court therefore reversed the circuit court's contrary judgment and remanded for further proceedings with respect to both appellant corporation's license revocation and the city's public nuisance claim. The court granted the corporation's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether this ordinance violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments and Ill. Const. art. I, § 4 (1970). The supreme court found that under the four-part test articulated in Ben's Bar, § 4-60-140(d) did not offend the First Amendment, as it was directed toward the regulation of alcohol sales and consumption in inappropriate locations, a matter within the city's general police powers. The experience of the city and other jurisdictions showed that the secondary harms to which § 4-60-140(d) were addressed were real and not merely conjectural. Section 4-60-140(d) was tailored precisely to its objective: combating the negative secondary effects flowing from the combination of nude or seminude dancing and alcohol sales. The corporation's argument that § 14-60-140(d) was invalid under Ill. Const. art. I, § 4 was rejected. Because the ordinance did not violate either the U.S. or the Illinois Constitution, the circuit court erred in concluding that the ordinance could not serve as the predicate for revoking the corporation's liquor license revocation or enjoining its operation on the grounds that it constituted a public nuisance. The appellate court therefore acted properly.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.
