People v. Woodrum


Docket No. 99984.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 286; 860 N.E.2d 259; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1633; 307 Ill. Dec. 605



October 5, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 5, 2006. Counsel Amended January 30, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Woodrum, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 2106 (Ill., Nov. 27, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Woodrum v. Illinois, 549 U.S. 1351, 127 S. Ct. 2058, 167 L. Ed. 2d 786, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 4140 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Woodrum, 354 Ill. App. 3d 629, 821 N.E.2d 787, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1535, 290 Ill. Dec. 475 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court reversed defendant's convictions on seven counts of child abduction in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-5(b)(10) (1998) after the trial court had found him guilty of those offenses following a bench trial. The State's petition for leave to appeal to the state supreme court was granted.


OVERVIEW: On two separate occasions, defendant lured children into his residence with the offer of viewing themselves on videotapes that he made of them. The children were eight and nine years old. The parents of the children did not consent. Defendant was charged with seven counts of child abduction in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-5(b)(10) (1998). That statute stated that the luring into a building of a child without parental consent was prima facie evidence of "other than a lawful purpose." The indictments stated that defendant's conduct in luring them into his residence without the consent of the parents was unlawful given that the children were under 16 years old. The State later amended the indictments to include the statements that defendant acted "for other than a lawful purpose." Defendant was convicted on all seven counts. On appeal, the appellate court reversed the convictions. On further review, the state supreme court found that the language that the luring shall be prima facie evidence of "other than a lawful purpose" was an unconstitutional mandatory rebuttable presumption but that the convictions were proper even absent the use of that presumption.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment regarding the convictions was reversed, and the trial court's judgments regarding them was affirmed.

 

193 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Molnar


Docket No. 100054.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


222 Ill. 2d 495; 857 N.E.2d 209; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1638; 306 Ill. Dec. 116



October 5, 2006, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault of a family member under the age of 18, was sentenced to four years' probation, and was required to register as a sex offender for 10 years. Defendant was charged with failure to register a change of address and giving a false address in his re-registration. The Circuit Court (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to dismiss and denied the State's motion to reconsider. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was subject to the registration requirement of the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, the Act was amended such that any person subject to the registration requirement who failed to register a change of address within 10 days or failed to register annually was subject to an increase in his or her registration requirement of 10 years. Defendant argued that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/7 (2004) and Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 1280.40 (2000) were unconstitutional because they did not require the state police to notify a registrant that he or she violated the Act, did not provide for notice of any proceeding where a registrant's period for reporting could be extended, did not provide a registrant with notice of the alleged reasons for the extension or with an opportunity to appear and contest the extension, and did not provide the registrant with notification that his or her registration period had been extended. The supreme court held that, as applied to defendant, the Act and Code satisfied due process. The Act and the Code clearly set forth defendant's duty to register, as well as defendant's responsibilities in the event defendant changed residence address.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

194 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


DeLuna v. Burciaga


Docket No. 101428.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 49; 857 N.E.2d 229; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1640; 306 Ill. Dec. 136



October 5, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
DeLuna v. Burciaga, 359 Ill. App. 3d 544, 834 N.E.2d 478, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 783, 295 Ill. Dec. 897 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the children of a decedent, filed a legal malpractice action against defendant attorney. The trial court granted the attorney's motion to dismiss the complaint. An Illinois appellate court reversed the dismissal and remanded the case. It held that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3(e) (2000) had not tolled the repose period for two plaintiffs, but found that there had been fraudulent concealment. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's husband retained the attorney to pursue a medical malpractice/wrongful death action. The children were then minors. The court first held that § 13-214.3(e) tolled the statutes of limitations and repose set forth in § 13-214.3(b) and (c). Thus, the legal malpractice suit was timely filed as to two plaintiffs, but whether it had been timely filed as to the other two depended on fraudulent concealment under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-215 (2000). There was no reason why § 13-215 should not apply to statutes of repose. A fiduciary who failed to disclose material facts concerning the existence of a cause of action had fraudulently concealed that action. As the underlying action had been brought for the benefit of the children, the attorney had owed them a fiduciary duty. Here, the children alleged that the attorney had fraudulently concealed the facts supporting the legal malpractice cause of action by failing to advise of the true status of the case, by representing that the case was going very well, and by stating that there was no need to contact him more frequently about its status. These allegations, if proven, were sufficient to establish fraudulent concealment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's finding that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3(e) had not tolled the statute of repose as to two plaintiffs. It affirmed the rest of the judgment of the appellate court. It reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Bridges v. State Bd. of Elections


Docket No. 102489.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


222 Ill. 2d 482; 856 N.E.2d 445; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1117; 305 Ill. Dec. 640



September 26, 2006, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed; mandate issued forthwith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that declared 2006 Ill. Laws 94-727, which amended the Circuit Courts Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 35/1 et seq., unconstitutional. Appellant state elections board and its members appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two counties were divided into separate judicial circuits by the Illinois General Assembly. Thereafter, the state elections board decreed that five new judgeships were required, three in one county and two in the other. Appellant candidates seeking to fill the new judgeships filed for the primary election. Before the primary, the Illinois General Assembly passed a law, 2006 Ill. Laws 94-727, in which it erased three of the additional judgeships. The candidates sued, and claimed, inter alia, that the action of the Illinois General Assembly violated the state constitution's separation of powers clause because the state elections board, part of the executive branch, allegedly had the power to determine how many judges an area should have. The trial court found that the law, 2006 Ill. Laws 94-727, which amended the Circuit Courts Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 35/1 et seq., was unconstitutional. On further review the state supreme court rejected the trial court's ruling. It found that the Illinois General Assembly had the constitutional authority to create a statute allowing for the creation of judgeships and, thus, likewise had the authority to rescind the creation of judgeships.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the mandate was issued forthwith.

Allegis Realty Investors v. Novak


Docket Nos. 100682, 100730 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


223 Ill. 2d 318; 860 N.E.2d 246; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1115; 307 Ill. Dec. 592



September 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Corrected January 30, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Allegis Realty Investors v. Novak, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 2105 (Ill., Nov. 27, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Allegis Realty Investors v. Novak, 550 U.S. 904, 127 S. Ct. 2100, 167 L. Ed. 2d 813, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 4363 (2007)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Allegis Realty Investors v. Novak, 379 Ill. App. 3d 636, 885 N.E.2d 325, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 177, 319 Ill. Dec. 54 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Allegis Realty Investors v. Novak, 356 Ill. App. 3d 887, 827 N.E.2d 485, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 26, 292 Ill. Dec. 956 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed objections under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/23-10 (1998) of the Property Tax Code to various taxes, including a permanent road tax. Intervenor road district intervened and moved for summary judgment. The motion was granted. The taxpayers brought an interlocutory appeal. The appellate court (Illinois) reversed and remanded. The supreme court granted defendant treasurer and the road district leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the supreme court was whether 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-620 could be applied retroactively to validate the tax levy challenged by the taxpayers. If § 6-620 applied retroactively, the supreme court concluded that the authorization obtained in 1979 for the road tax levy did not expire and the challenged 1997 levy was not subject to challenge on the ground that it failed to comply with 60 Ill. Comp. stat. Ann. 1/30-20(b) (1998). The supreme court held that 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-620 could be applied retroactively. The statute cured the defects on which the taxpayers' challenge was based. No after-the-fact declaration of intent was made concerning the preamendatory law and no final judgment was disturbed. Prior to the instant action, the specific taxes at issue had been invalidated by a court of law. In addition, the taxes validated were not limited to plaintiff taxpayers. Thus, retroactive application of the curative statute was permissible and did not violate the principles of separation of powers or deprive the taxpayers of their rights to due process under the Illinois or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed. The circuit court's judgment was affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

197 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. M.T. (In re M.T.)


Docket No. 99310.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


221 Ill. 2d 517; 852 N.E.2d 792; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1093; 304 Ill. Dec. 336



June 22, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 23, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. M.T. (In re M.T.), 352 Ill. App. 3d 131, 816 N.E.2d 354, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1001, 287 Ill. Dec. 592 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court, in a case where the trial court adjudicated respondent minor delinquent after a judicial determination that he had violated the indecent solicitation of an adult statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6.5(a) (2000), held that the statute violated the state constitution's proportionate penalties clause and found the entire statute unconstitutional. The State appealed and the minor cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The minor arranged for another minor to received oral sex from another student who was an adult and the other student performed that sex act on the other minor because the other student believed that if she didn't, the minor would physically harm her. The minor was adjudicated delinquent following a judicial determination that he had violated the indecent solicitation of an adult statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6.5(a) (2000). The appellate court held that the statute violated the proportionate penalties clause of the state constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, based on its use of cross-comparison analysis and found the entire statute unconstitutional. The State appealed; the minor cross-appealed. The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment because it no longer applied the cross-comparison analysis in proportionate penalties cases following its Sharpe decision. It also agreed with the appellate court that the statute applied equally to adult and juvenile offenders, and that the statute did not violate the minor's due process rights. Also, the state supreme court found that the minor had standing to raise the due process challenge.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court held that the appellate court's judgment was reversed and that the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

198 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Waid


Docket No. 101065.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


221 Ill. 2d 464; 851 N.E.2d 1210; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1080; 303 Ill. Dec. 785



June 2, 2006, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pike County Circuit Court (Illinois) denied the State's motion for admission of evidence, which effectively found that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/104-25(a) was unconstitutional, where defendant was charged with drug and alcohol-related crimes, he was found mentally unfit to stand trial and unlikely to be fit within one year, and the State moved for a discharge hearing under that statute to determine evidence sufficiency. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with various drug and alcohol-related offenses in four separate cases. Prior to trial, on his motion, the trial court found defendant mentally unfit to stand trial. It also found that there was no substantial probability that defendant would attain fitness within one year. The State moved for a discharge hearing pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/104-25(a) (2004) to determine the sufficiency of the evidence against defendant. The State also moved, pursuant to that section, for the admission of certain evidence. The trial court denied the State's motion for admission of evidence, effectively finding 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/104-25(a) (2004) unconstitutional. On appeal, the state supreme court found that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/104-25(a) (2004) was constitutional. It found that a discharge hearing was a civil proceeding, and, thus, defendant's confrontation clause rights were not implicated. It also found that due process in regard to a discharge proceeding did not protect him like it would in a criminal trial, and, thus, his constitutional rights were not violated by that statute allowing the admission of hearsay or affidavit evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

199 of 2788 DOCUMENTS



Davis v. Brown


Docket No. 100624.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


221 Ill. 2d 435; 851 N.E.2d 1198; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1082; 303 Ill. Dec. 773



June 2, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davis v. Brown, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8060 (U.S., Oct. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
Davis v. Brown, 357 Ill. App. 3d 176, 827 N.E.2d 508, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 372, 292 Ill. Dec. 979 (Ill. App. Ct., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court ruled, inter alia, that 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-510 (2004), which permitted appellee state transportation agency to prepare and record maps setting forth a right-of-way for a proposed highway, was facially constitutional. Appellant property owners appealed that ruling.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois Highway Code, 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-510 (2004), authorized the state transportation agency to prepare and record maps that established the approximate locations and widths of rights of way for future state highway system additions. Pursuant to that statute, the state transportation agency prepared and recorded a map that set forth a right-of-way for a proposed highway. The property owners, whose property fell within the right-of-way, filed an action for declaratory judgment, seeking to have that statute declared unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint, primarily because it believed that the property owners lacked standing. On appeal, the appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment that property owners lacked standing, but rejected their constitutional arguments on the merits. On further review and since the state transportation agency conceded that there was standing, the state supreme court found that only the constitutionality of the statute remained as an issue and further ruled that the statute did not violate the federal takings clause, state separation of powers principles, or substantive due process principles.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.


 

200 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Caballes


Docket No. 91547


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


221 Ill. 2d 282; 851 N.E.2d 26; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 625; 303 Ill. Dec. 128



May 18, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 23, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Caballes, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1096 (Ill., June 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District.
People v. Caballes, 321 Ill. App. 3d 1063, 797 N.E.2d 250, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1248, 277 Ill. Dec. 903 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the U.S. Supreme Court, the court reconsidered issues related to defendant's case, in which he was convicted of cannabis trafficking by an Illinois circuit court after a trained dog alerted to the presence of marijuana in the trunk of defendant's car. The appellate court affirmed, and the instant court reversed.


OVERVIEW: The court was asked to reconsider its long-standing position, known as the "limited lockstep doctrine," that the search and seizure clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 (1970) should be interpreted in the same manner as the virtually identical search and seizure clause of the Fourth Amendment. The court reaffirmed its commitment to limited lockstep analysis not only because it felt constrained to do so by the doctrine of stare decisis, but because the limited lockstep approach continued to reflect the court's understanding of the intent of the framers of the Illinois Constitution of 1970. Defendant argued that, notwithstanding the United States Supreme Court's interpretation of the search and seizure clause of the Fourth Amendment, the court should consider a canine sniff to be a "search," within the meaning of Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. However, in light of the continued adherence to the lockstep doctrine, albeit with some room for flexibility, defendant had not made a case for an exception to the lockstep doctrine. Given the limited lockstep approach to search and seizure analysis, the sniff did not violate defendant's right to be free from unreasonable search and seizure.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court, which affirmed the circuit court's judgment, was affirmed.
